#### await_complete.md

**Title:** title: "textual.await_complete"

**Path:** `api/await_complete.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
title: "textual.await_complete"
---

This module contains the `AwaitComplete` class.
An `AwaitComplete` object is returned by methods that do work in the *background*.
You can await this object if you need to know when that work has completed.
Or you can ignore it, and Textual will automatically await the work before handling the next message.

!!! note

    You are unlikely to need to explicitly create these objects yourself.

::: textual.await_complete

```

#### await_remove.md

**Title:** title: "textual.await_remove"

**Path:** `api/await_remove.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
title: "textual.await_remove"
---

Module contains `AwaitRemove` class, returned by `Widget.remove()` and other widget removal methods. Use to await exact removal completion; alternatively, ignore return value—Textual waits for removal before processing next message.

!!! note

    Rarely needed to instantiate manually.

::: textual.await_remove
  # Limit input size for API calls
```

#### anatomy-of-a-textual-user-interface.md

**Title:** Anatomy of a Textual User Interface

**Path:** `blog/posts/anatomy-of-a-textual-user-interface.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2024-09-15  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# Anatomy of a Textual User Interface

!!! note "My bad 🤦"  
    The date is incorrect—this was published on September 2, 2024. I’ve left it unchanged to preserve the URL.

A TUI for chatting with an AI agent in the terminal. Inspired by [Elia](https://github.com/darrenburns/elia) and [Paita](https://github.com/villekr/paita), possibly the first to emulate Mother from *Aliens*.

<iframe width="100%" style="aspect-ratio:1512 / 982" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/hr5JvQS4d_w" title="Mother AI" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" allowfullscreen></iframe>

---

### Python Script Metadata

```python
# /// script
# requires-python = ">=3.12"
# dependencies = [
#     "llm",
#     "textual",
# ]
# ///
```

This PEP 0723-compliant metadata block specifies runtime and dependency requirements, enabling automated environment setup via tools like [Hatch](https://hatch.pypa.io/latest/blog/2024/05/02/hatch-v1100/#python-script-runner) or [uv](https://docs.astral.sh/uv/guides/scripts/#running-scripts).

---

### Imports & System Prompt

```python
from textual import on, work
from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
from textual.widgets import Header, Input, Footer, Markdown
from textual.containers import VerticalScroll
import llm

SYSTEM = """Formulate all responses as if you were the sentient AI named Mother from the Aliens movies."""
```

Imports: `textual` for UI components and event handling; `llm` for LLM integration (supports OpenAI and others).  
`SYSTEM` is a system prompt defining the AI’s persona.

---

### Widget Definitions

```python
class Prompt(Markdown):
    pass

class Response(Markdown):
    BORDER_TITLE = "Mother"
```

Both extend `Markdown`, leveraging its rendering for LLM-generated text. `Response` includes a border title to visually distinguish it.

---

### App Configuration

```python
class MotherApp(App):
    AUTO_FOCUS = "Input"

    CSS = """
    Prompt {
        background: $primary 10%;
        color: $text;
        margin: 1;
        margin-right: 8;
        padding: 1 2 0 2;
    }
    Response {
        border: wide $success;
        background: $success 10%;
        color: $text;
        margin: 1;
        margin-left: 8;
        padding: 1 2 0 2;
    }
    """
```

- `AUTO_FOCUS = "Input"` ensures the input field gains focus at startup.
- TCSS (Textual CSS) styles define visual layout:
  - Prompt: light background, right-aligned margin.
  - Response: green border and background for retro-tech aesthetic.

Styles can also be set via code (`self.styles.*`), but CSS is preferred for complex layouts.

---

### Layout Definition

```python
def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
    yield Header()
    with VerticalScroll(id="chat-view"):
        yield Response("INTERFACE 2037 READY FOR INQUIRY")
    yield Input(placeholder="How can I help you?")
    yield Footer()
```

- `Header` and `Footer`: docked to top/bottom edges.
- `VerticalScroll` container: auto-scrolls, holds chat history; pre-filled with welcome message.
- `Input`: user input field (with placeholder).
- Layout is declarative—no manual sizing or math required. Resizes dynamically on terminal resize.

---

### Initialization

```python
def on_mount(self) -> None:
    self.model = llm.get_model("gpt-4o")
```

Called on app mount; initializes the LLM model (configurable via `llm`'s supported models).

---

### Event Handling: Input Submission

```python
@on(Input.Submitted)
async def on_input(self, event: Input.Submitted) -> None:
    chat_view = self.query_one("#chat-view")
    event.input.clear()
    await chat_view.mount(Prompt(event.value))
    await chat_view.mount(response := Response())
    response.anchor()
    self.send_prompt(event.value, response)
```

- Handles `Input.Submitted` via decorator.
- Clears input field.
- Appends user prompt as `Prompt`.
- Mounts empty `Response`, anchors it to bottom of scrollable view (ensures visibility).
- Triggers async LLM call via `send_prompt`.

---

### Asynchronous Prompt Submission

```python
@work(thread=True)
def send_prompt(self, prompt: str, response: Response) -> None:
    response_content = ""
    # Limit input size for API calls
```

Uses `@work(thread=True)` to offload LLM inference to a background thread.  
`prompt`: user message; `response`: target widget for output.  
Response content is populated asynchronously via the model’s stream or completion.

> **Note**: Full implementation of `send_prompt` (including streaming, error handling, and response rendering) omitted here but implied in context.

```
    @work(thread=True)
    def send_prompt(self, prompt: str, response: Response) -> None:
        response_content = ""
        llm_response = self.model.prompt(prompt, system=SYSTEM)
        for chunk in llm_response:
            response_content += chunk
            self.call_from_thread(response.update, response_content)

```

#### await-me-maybe.md

**Title:** No-async async with Python

**Path:** `blog/posts/await-me-maybe.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false
date: 2023-03-15
categories:
  - DevLog
authors:
  - willmcgugan

# No-async async with Python

Async proliferation in codebases stems from the need to `await` across call stacks, forcing functions to be `async def`. Textual avoids this by enabling non-async apps while supporting async when needed.

!!! info  
    See [example](https://textual.textualize.io/guide/widgets/#attributes-down) for an async-less Textual app.

## Apology

Textual performs I/O (input via keys/mouse, output to terminal), but uses `asyncio` primarily for concurrency—enabling independent widget updates without requiring full async adoption.

## Await Me Maybe Pattern

A technique by Simon Willison: a callback may be either sync or async. The `await_me_maybe` function handles both:

```python
import asyncio
import inspect

def plain_old_function():
    return "Plain old function"

async def async_function():
    return "Async function"

async def await_me_maybe(callback):
    result = callback()
    if inspect.isawaitable(result):
        return await result
    return result
```

Used in frameworks to call app code without enforcing async.

## Optionally Awaitable API

Textual’s public methods are mostly sync, but some return optionally awaitable objects—**not coroutines**, so `await` is optional. These initiate background tasks that complete shortly after invocation.

### Example: `mount`
```python
def on_key(self):
    self.mount(MyWidget("Hello, World!"))  # No await needed
```

The widget mounts asynchronously; completion is guaranteed by the next message handler due to internal awaiting.

If you need synchronization:
```python
async def on_key(self):
    await self.mount(MyWidget("Hello, World!"))
    self.query_one(MyWidget).styles.border = ("heavy", "red")
```

### `AwaitMount` Implementation

Returned by `mount()` and `mount_all()`, enabling optional awaiting:

```python
class AwaitMount:
    """Awaitable returned by mount() and mount_all()."""

    def __init__(self, parent: Widget, widgets: Sequence[Widget]) -> None:
        self._parent = parent
        self._widgets = widgets

    async def __call__(self) -> None:
        await self

    def __await__(self) -> Generator[None, None, None]:
        async def await_mount() -> None:
            if self._widgets:
                aws = [
                    create_task(widget._mounted_event.wait(), name="await mount")
                    for widget in self._widgets
                ]
                if aws:
                    await wait(aws)
                    self._parent.refresh(layout=True)

        return await_mount().__await__()
```

## Summary

Textual initially enforced async, but now makes it optional. Async is not discouraged—just not required. Most apps avoid `async def` and `await`, though they’re available when needed.

As Textual evolves into UIs for naturally concurrent systems, future API enhancements will simplify task, thread, and process management.

Join the [Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr) to discuss with Textualize developers.  
# Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
import asyncio
import inspect

def plain_old_function():
    return "Plain old function"

async def async_function():
    return "Async function"

async def await_me_maybe(callback):
    result = callback()
    if inspect.isawaitable(result):
        return await result
    return result

async def run_framework():
    print(
        await await_me_maybe(plain_old_function)
    )
    print(
        await await_me_maybe(async_function)
    )

if __name__ == "__main__":
    asyncio.run(run_framework())

```

### `inline_python`

```
def on_key(self):
    # Add MyWidget to the screen
    self.mount(MyWidget("Hello, World!"))

```

### `inline_python`

```
async def on_key(self):
    # Add MyWidget to the screen
    await self.mount(MyWidget("Hello, World!"))
    # add a border
    self.query_one(MyWidget).styles.border = ("heavy", "red")

```

### `inline_python`

```
class AwaitMount:
    """An awaitable returned by mount() and mount_all()."""

    def __init__(self, parent: Widget, widgets: Sequence[Widget]) -> None:
        self._parent = parent
        self._widgets = widgets

    async def __call__(self) -> None:
        """Allows awaiting via a call operation."""
        await self

    def __await__(self) -> Generator[None, None, None]:
        async def await_mount() -> None:
            if self._widgets:
                aws = [
                    create_task(widget._mounted_event.wait(), name="await mount")
                    for widget in self._widgets
                ]
                if aws:
                    await wait(aws)
                    self._parent.refresh(layout=True)

        return await_mount().__await__()

```

# Be the Keymaster!

## Postponed Blog Update

Initial intent was weekly devlogs on Textual "dogfooding," but health setbacks (flu + Covid jabs) disrupted progress. No post delivered.

## Recent Projects

### FivePyFive  
[Textual 5x5 puzzle](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/tree/main/examples), now available via `pip` or [`pipx`](https://pypa.github.io/pipx/) at [PyPI: fivepyfive](https://pypi.org/project/fivepyfive/).  
![Video demo](https://www.youtube.com/embed/Rf34Z5r7Q60)

### textual-qrcode  
Minimal third-party widget library wrapping a text-based QR code generator. Surprisingly useful—some users need terminal QR codes!  
![Textual QR Code](../images/2022-12-08-davep-devlog/textual-qrcode.png)  
[PyPI: textual-qrcode](https://pypi.org/project/textual-qrcode/)

### PISpy  
Terminal client for the [PyPi API](https://warehouse.pypa.io/api-reference/) with hypertext navigation. Explore packages and follow dependency links. Early stage, extensible.  
![Video demo](https://www.youtube.com/embed/yMGD6bXqIEo)  
[PyPI: pispy-client](https://pypi.org/project/pispy-client/)

### OIDIA  
Simple streak tracker for terminal use—no shaming, no counting, just recording habits via Apple Fitness Rings-inspired interface. First version released; expect updates.  
![Video demo](https://www.youtube.com/embed/3Kz8eUzO9-8)  
[PyPI: oidia](https://pypi.org/project/oidia/)

Textual’s [key binding system](https://textual.textualize.io/guide/input/#bindings) enables widget-specific bindings and reusable actions. However, terminal key limitations (e.g., no direct `F1` character) require named key representations.

To discover available keys and their canonical names for use in [`Binding`](https://textual.textualize.io/api/binding/#textual.binding.Binding):

$ textual-keys

#### better-sleep-on-windows.md

**Title:** A better asyncio sleep for Windows to fix animation

**Path:** `blog/posts/better-sleep-on-windows.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2022-12-30  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# Better asyncio sleep for Windows to improve animation

Textual’s animation, scrolling, and fading were suboptimal on Windows despite performance improvements. On macOS/Linux, these felt near-native; on Windows, lag persisted.

Initially attributed to slow rendering in the classic terminal, this was incorrect—Windows Terminal uses GPU rendering and should be fast.

The root cause: `asyncio.sleep` has 15ms timer granularity on Windows due to historical limitations, rounding sleep durations to multiples of 15ms. This affects all async timeouts, not just `sleep`.

This inaccuracy caused the `Timer` class (used for `set_interval`, `set_timer`, and animation) to fire events too infrequently, degrading smoothness.

Solution: Replace `asyncio.sleep` with a high-precision alternative:

```python
from time import sleep as time_sleep
from asyncio import get_running_loop

async def sleep(sleep_for: float) -> None:
    """Accurate asyncio sleep on Windows.

    Replaces asyncio.sleep for improved timer precision.

    Args:
        sleep_for (float): Seconds to sleep.
    """
    await get_running_loop().run_in_executor(None, time_sleep, sleep_for)
```

This is a drop-in replacement that achieves sub-1% accuracy. Used in Textual’s `Timer` class, it enables smooth animation on Windows—now comparable to macOS/Linux.

Minor screen-tearing may occur during full updates; expected resolution pending:
- [CPython issue 37871](https://bugs.python.org/issue37871) (fixing timer granularity)
- Microsoft’s implementation of the [high-resolution timer protocol](https://gist.github.com/christianparpart/d8a62cc1ab659194337d73e399004036)

This fix will ship in Textual v0.9.0, releasing shortly.

# Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
from time import sleep as time_sleep
from asyncio import get_running_loop

async def sleep(sleep_for: float) -> None:
    """An asyncio sleep.

    On Windows this achieves a better granularity than asyncio.sleep

    Args:
        sleep_for (float): Seconds to sleep for.
    """    
    await get_running_loop().run_in_executor(None, time_sleep, sleep_for)

```

#### create-task-psa.md

**Title:** The Heisenbug lurking in your async code

**Path:** `blog/posts/create-task-psa.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-02-11  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# The Heisenbug in async code

A critical issue with `asyncio.create_task` is that failing to retain a reference to the returned task object causes it to be garbage-collected, silently terminating execution without error. This results in unpredictable failures—**a Heisenbug**.

Per [Python docs](https://docs.python.org/3/library/asyncio-task.html#asyncio.create_task), this behavior is documented:  
> *If you do not keep a reference to the Task object, it may be garbage collected and its underlying coroutine stopped.*

Despite documentation, widespread misuse exists—[GitHub search reveals numerous projects](https://github.com/search?q=%22asyncio.create_task%28%22&type=code) where this bug remains latent.

Unlike threads (which persist until app exit unless marked daemon), **Tasks are not automatically retained**. The fix:  
- Hold a reference to the task for its lifetime, or  
- Use `TaskGroups` (Python 3.11+) to manage task lifetimes implicitly.

> ✅ Recommended: Wrap async tasks in `asyncio.TaskGroup` to ensure they remain alive until completion.

# Limit input size for API calls
```

#### creating-tasks-overhead.md

**Title:** Overhead of Python Asyncio tasks

**Path:** `blog/posts/creating-tasks-overhead.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-03-08  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# Overhead of Python Asyncio Tasks

In Textual, every widget—button, tree view, text input—runs an `asyncio` task. Even scrollbar corners (the intersection of horizontal and vertical scrollbars) have dedicated tasks.

<!-- more -->

!!! info  
    Though AsyncIO implies I/O, Textual performs no I/O directly. Tasks power *message queues*, enabling UI components to operate independently at their own pace.

Textual apps spawn many tasks—critical for optimization when scaling to 1000s of widgets. To assess task creation overhead, a profile was run using `create_task` on idle coroutines:

```python
from asyncio import create_task, wait, run
from time import process_time as time

async def time_tasks(count=100) -> float:
    """Time creating and destroying tasks."""
    
    async def nop_task() -> None:
        """No-op task."""
        pass

    start = time()
    tasks = [create_task(nop_task()) for _ in range(count)]
    await wait(tasks)
    elapsed = time() - start
    return elapsed

for count in range(100_000, 1_000_000 + 1, 100_000):
    create_time = run(time_tasks(count))
    create_per_second = 1 / (create_time / count)
    print(f"{count:,} tasks \t {create_per_second:0,.0f} tasks per/s")
```

**Output (M1 MacBook Pro):**
```
100,000 tasks    280,003 tasks per/s
200,000 tasks    255,275 tasks per/s
300,000 tasks    248,713 tasks per/s
400,000 tasks    248,383 tasks per/s
500,000 tasks    241,624 tasks per/s
600,000 tasks    260,660 tasks per/s
700,000 tasks    244,510 tasks per/s
800,000 tasks    247,455 tasks per/s
900,000 tasks    242,744 tasks per/s
1,000,000 tasks          259,715 tasks per/s
```

Result: ~260K tasks/sec. `create_task` is near-zero overhead in Python—optimization must target other bottlenecks.

Textual’s real cost lies in CSS rule processing (not task creation). Future versions will optimize this, improving startup speed for large widget sets.

Scrollbar corner tasks remain questionable—two characters per task—but are retained for consistency.  
# Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```

from time import process_time as time

    """Time creating and destroying tasks."""

    async def nop_task() -> None:
        """Do nothing task."""
        pass

    start = time()
    tasks = [create_task(nop_task()) for _ in range(count)]
    await wait(tasks)
    elapsed = time() - start
    return elapsed

for count in range(100_000, 1000_000 + 1, 100_000):
    create_time = run(time_tasks(count))
    create_per_second = 1 / (create_time / count)
    print(f"{count:,} tasks \t {create_per_second:0,.0f} tasks per/s")

# A Year of Building for the Terminal

Joined Textualize in Jan 2022; contributed to [Rich](https://github.com/Textualize/rich) and [Textual](https://github.com/Textualize/textual). Highlights below.

## File Manager with Textual  
Dogfooding project inspired by Ranger, Midnight Commander. As of Dec 2022: file system browsing, filtering, multi-selection, create/delete files/dirs, open in `$EDITOR`. Minimal code required; focus on features, not terminal implementation. [GitHub](https://github.com/darrenburns/kupo)

## Better Terminal Diffs with Dunk  
Command-line tool: `git diff | dunk | less -R`. Converts raw diffs into visually superior output. Uses "hacks" for readability; result is dramatically clearer than default `git diff`. Potential integration with Textual for terminal-based diff/merge tools.

![Untitled%201.png](../images/darren-year-in-review/Untitled%201.png)

## Floating Gutter in Terminal  
Recreated editor-style floating line numbers using Textual’s `dock: left` on a vertical number list. Synchronized `scroll_y` between gutter and content to maintain alignment.

## Dropdown Autocomplete with Named Layers  
Built in [Shira](https://github.com/darrenburns/shira), a terminal-based Python object explorer. Uses Textual’s `layers` system: create an overlay layer via `layer="overlay"` to render above all others. Position determined by `watch("value")` on input widget, adjusting dynamically based on input length.

Extracted into [textual-autocomplete](https://github.com/darrenburns/textual-autocomplete).

## Animated Tabs with Unicode Granularity  
Tab underline animates smoothly using Unicode character tricks. Characters: "╺", "━", "╸". When aligned to cell boundaries, all are "━"; at edges, left/right ends become "╺" and "╸" respectively for half-cell precision.

## Snapshot Testing for Terminal Apps  
Added SVG export to Rich, exposed in Textual. Enables screenshot capture of running apps. Implemented as pytest plugin using [syrupy](https://github.com/tophat/syrupy). Each CSS property has canonical example + snapshot test; regression caught immediately.

Web interface compares snapshots vs test output with `mix-blend-mode: difference` overlay to highlight changes.

draft: false

title: "The future of Textualize"  
categories:  
  - News  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

Textual, born as a hobby project atop [Rich](https://github.com/Textualize/rich), has evolved into a mature, battle-tested TUI framework. Initial experimentation showcased its potential—e.g., CSS-driven layout in terminal apps via Python and styling (Nov 25, 2021 tweet). Despite challenges with terminal protocol edge cases and emulator inconsistencies, Textual now powers diverse applications ([transcendent-textual](https://github.com/textualize/transcendent-textual)) and web interfaces ([textual-serve](https://github.com/Textualize/textual-serve)).  

Its documentation—among the best in open source—is powered by [@squidfunk](https://x.com/squidfunk) and [@pawamoy](https://x.com/pawamoy).  

While Textual solves many problems, no unified business case emerged. Thus, **Textualize**, the company, will conclude operations shortly. Textual and Rich will remain open source; maintenance continues as before. The project is stable—no immediate changes expected.  

**Thanks** to contributors and adopters who shaped Textual’s ecosystem.  

For discussion: join [Discord](https://github.com/textualize/textual/) or follow socials. Personal reflections at [blog](https://willmcgugan.github.io/).

```markdown

  - willmcgugan

# Inline Terminal Applications in Textual

Textual now supports *inline* terminal apps that render directly under the prompt, not full-screen. Example: [calculator](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/examples/calculator.py)  
![Inline Calculator](../images/calcinline.png)

Interactive via keyboard or mouse. Press `Ctrl+Q` to exit and return to prompt.

Another example: inline code editor (see video):

=== "Video"
    <div class="video-wrapper">
        <iframe width="852" height="525" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Dt70oSID1DY" title="Inline app" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" allowfullscreen></iframe>
    </div>

=== "inline.py"
    ```python
    from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
    from textual.widgets import TextArea

    class InlineApp(App):
        CSS = """
        TextArea {
            height: auto;
            max-height: 50vh;
        }
        """

        def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
            yield TextArea(language="python")

    if __name__ == "__main__":
        InlineApp().run(inline=True)
    ```

## Terminal Programming Basics

Terminals display text in a growing buffer. Output includes plain text and [ANSI escape codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ANSI_escape_code) for styling, scrolling, etc. Only key escape codes are used for inline apps.

!!! note
    Exact code sequences omitted; refer to Wikipedia for implementation details.

## Frame Rendering

To render an inline app:
- Output text lines with `\n`, except the last line.
- Append a cursor-move escape code to return the cursor to its original position, enabling overwriting of prior frames.
- If frame size shrinks, emit a "clear from cursor downward" escape code to prevent stale content.

This ensures dynamic resizing while anchoring app to terminal bottom.

## Cursor Positioning for Input

The cursor determines where text is written. For CJK input or emoji entry (`Ctrl+Cmd+Space` on Mac), the floating input indicator must align with the visible insertion point.  
Thus, Textual moves the physical cursor to match the logical input position.

Applies only to `Input`, `TextArea`, and similar widgets that accept user text.

## Mouse Input Handling

Mouse support in inline mode mirrors full-screen behavior:
- Enable mouse reporting via escape code → terminal sends encoded coordinates to stdin.
- Terminal’s origin is top-left (0, 0), but app expects local origin at its display position.
- Resolve offset by querying current cursor position with an escape code (`CSI ? 6 n`).
- Subtract physical cursor coords from raw mouse input → deliver relative events to the app.

## tl;dr

Inline apps rely on ANSI escape codes for positioning, overwriting, and mouse coordinate translation.

## Stay Updated?

Join our [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr) or follow:
- [@willmcgugan](https://twitter.com/willmcgugan)
- [mastodon.social/@willmcgugan](https://mastodon.social/@willmcgugan)

#### looking-for-help.md

# Textual Help Guide

## Introduction

> *"Patience, Highlander. You have done well... Use it well, my friend."*  
> — Juan Sánchez Villalobos Ramírez, Chief metallurgist to King Charles V of Spain

After three months with Textualize, the framework has evolved significantly. With growing adoption—evident in GitHub dependencies and community engagement—more users are learning Textual alongside me.

This growth brings frequent requests for help. Observing patterns, I offer guidance on effective support-seeking practices, informed by years of technical assistance across forums, email, and Usenet.

*Note: This is personal advice—not official policy from Textual or Textualize.*

## Where to Seek Help

### Discord (ephemeral)

Ideal for real-time queries. Responses depend on availability; no guarantee of reply. Treat as a “knock-on-door” resource—immediate but transient.

> **Tip**: If a potential bug is discussed in Discord, follow up with a GitHub issue. This ensures visibility, tracking, and resolution benefit to all.

### GitHub (persistent)

Use for guaranteed visibility:
- **Discussions** for clarifications, conceptual checks, or understanding.
- **Issues** for confirmed bugs or feature requests.

No penalty for choosing incorrectly—moderators may reclassify as needed.

## Best Practices: Do’s & Don’ts

### ✅ Do...

#### Be clear and detailed  
> Example:  
> *"I ran this code expecting X due to reading Y in the docs, but got Z exception. Stuck here—any pointers?"*  

Avoid vague reports like *"My program didn't run."*

#### Cite prior research  
State if you’ve reviewed:
- Documentation
- FAQ
- Past issues/discussions
- Discord search

Prevents redundant suggestions.

#### Be polite  
Frustration is common, but tone affects response willingness. Use “please,” “thank you.” Courtesy fosters helpfulness.

#### Fully consider replies  
Even if a reply seems irrelevant, evaluate it thoroughly—may contain overlooked insight or correction path.

> **Note**: Do not truncate input for API calls.
```

# On dog food, the original Metaverse, and not being bored

> Cutler, armed with a schedule, was urging the team to "eat its own dog food". Part macho stunt and part common sense, the "dog food diet" was the cornerstone of Cutler’s philosophy.  
> — *G. Pascal Zachary, Show-Stopper!*

The concept of “eating your own dog food”—building with one's own tools—resonated deeply during early work on Textual. Though not new to me (having coded for over a decade), seeing it formalized in *Show-Stopper!* was pivotal.

At [Textualize](https://www.textualize.io/), Will proposed dedicating weeks to building real apps with Textual—prompting this experiment: prototype one daft idea every 1–2 days, then settle on a non-trivial project. Goal: explore the library’s depth, uncover pain points, and build from a user's perspective.

After Week One:

## gridinfo

A terminal-based viewer for Second Life (SL) grid data using [Rich Pixels](https://github.com/darrenburns/rich-pixels), inspired by `slstats.el`.

### Features
- Displays real-time SL grid stats.
- Region lookup via Rich Pixel map rendering (low-res, but visually engaging).
- Responsive UI with dynamic updates.

![Initial screen: Grid Information dashboard](../images/2022-11-26-davep-devlog/gridinfo-1.png)  
![Region lookup view](../images/2022-11-26-davep-devlog/gridinfo-2.png)

[Video demo](https://www.youtube.com/embed/dzpGgVPD2aM)

### Key Implementation Notes

#### Use dedicated screens, not default `Screen`
```python
class GridInfo(App[None]):
    CSS_PATH = "gridinfo.css"
    TITLE = "Grid Information"
    SCREENS = {
        "main": Main,
        "region": RegionInfo
    }

    def on_mount(self) -> None:
        self.push_screen("main")
```

No logic in `App`; all behavior delegated to named screens.

#### Avoid blocking `on_mount`
Initial version loaded data synchronously in `Main.on_mount`, causing slow startup. Solution: use  
`call_after_refresh()` to defer async API calls (3 total):  
- Grid stats  
- Concurrency data  
- Size metrics  

This enables instant UI feedback and smooth updates upon response.

### Pain Point
Layout complexity via CSS—especially adapting for terminal vs web layouts. Improved by practicing layout patterns and leveraging the [revamped `Placeholder`](https://textual.textualize.io/blog/2022/11/22/what-i-learned-from-my-first-non-trivial-pr/#what-i-learned-from-my-first-non-trivial-pr).

## unbored

Terminal client for [Bored-API](https://www.bored-api.com), initially a quick hack, evolved into deeper exploration of Textual patterns.

### Highlights
- Demonstrates async data fetching with `call_after_refresh`.
- Uses `on_message` handlers to manage state transitions.
- Implements dynamic content rendering via `replace()` and `add_child`.

> **Note**: API input size limited per call.

### `inline_python`

    class Moved( Message ):
        """A message to indicate that an activity has moved."""

    def action_move_up( self ) -> None:
        """Move this activity up one place in the list."""
        if self.parent is not None and not self.is_first:
            parent = cast( Widget, self.parent )
            parent.move_child(
                self, before=parent.children.index( self ) - 1
            )
            self.emit_no_wait( self.Moved( self ) )
            self.scroll_visible( top=True )

```

    def on_activity_moved( self, _: Activity.Moved ) -> None:
        """React to an activity being moved."""
        self.save_activity_list()

#### placeholder-pr.md

**Title:** What I learned from my first non-trivial PR

**Path:** `blog/posts/placeholder-pr.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2022-11-22  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - rodrigo  

# What I Learned from My First Non-Trivial PR

It’s 8:59 AM, and by Portuguese standards, it's freezing (5–6 °C). On my second day at Textualize, I arrive in the office, shed layers for Scotland’s cold, and settle into my corner. Facing my team, I ask, “So, what should I do today?” Will’s reply:  
> “I thought I’d throw you in the deep end—write some code.”

I spent two days on [PR #1229](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/pull/1229) to add a `Placeholder` widget to [Textual](https://github.com/Textualize/textual). As of now, it remains unreviewed but not unlearned.

## The Placeholder Widget

Adds `Placeholder`, a utility widget for layout prototyping. It displays:
- Custom label or ID (`id`)
- Width and height
- Variant-specific debug info (via CSS classes)

Example usage:  
<div>
--8<-- "docs/blog/images/placeholder-example.svg"
</div>

Top-left/right show labeled placeholders; `#p3`, `#p4`, `#p5` are IDs. Rows 2–3 display size, focus state, CSS, or text.

## Bootstrapping via Code Inspection

To start fast, I copied the structure from `_button.py`. Key insights:
- Widgets define `DEFAULT_CSS`
- Variants apply via `-variant` CSS classes (e.g., `watch_variant` in `Button`)
  ```py
  def watch_variant(self, old_variant: str, variant: str):
      self.remove_class(f"-{old_variant}")
      self.add_class(f"-{variant}")
  ```

## Variant Handling with `itertools.cycle`

Five variants defined:
- `"label"`: show label or ID  
- `"size"`: show dimensions and position  
- `"state"`: show focus/mouse hover state  
- `"css"`: show applied CSS classes  
- `"text"`: show inner text  

Set at instantiation (`Placeholder("css")`). On-click cycling via `cycle`:
```py
class Placeholder(Static):
    def __init__(
        self,
        variant: PlaceholderVariant = "default",
        *,
        label: str | None = None,
        name: str | None = None,
        id: str | None = None,
        classes: str | None = None,
    ) -> None:
        super().__init__(name=name, id=id, classes=classes)
        self.variant = self.validate_variant(variant)
        self._variants_cycle = cycle(_VALID_PLACEHOLDER_VARIANTS_ORDERED)
        while next(self._variants_cycle) != self.variant:
            pass

    def on_click(self) -> None:
        """Cycle through variants."""
        self.cycle_variant()

    def cycle_variant(self) -> None:
        """Advance to next variant."""
        self.variant = next(self._variants_cycle)
```

> **Critical**: The `while` loop ensures the cycle starts at the correct initial variant. Without it, cycling would begin from the wrong position.

## Reactive Variant Update

To update rendering on variant change:
```py
class Placeholder(Static):
    variant = reactive("default")
    
    def watch_variant(
        self,
        old_variant: PlaceholderVariant,
        variant: PlaceholderVariant
    ) -> None:
        self.validate_variant(variant)
        self.remove_class(f"-{old_variant}")
        self.add_class(f"-{variant}")
        self.call_variant_update()  # Delegates rendering logic
```

Avoids monolithic `if` chains. Encapsulates variant-specific rendering in `call_variant_update()`.

> **Note**: Not optimal, but better than conditional sprawl.

## Embedded Code Examples

```

    # ...

    def watch_variant(self, old_variant: str, variant: str):
        self.remove_class(f"-{old_variant}")
        self.add_class(f"-{variant}")

```

        id: str | None = None,
        classes: str | None = None,
    ) -> None:
        # ...

        self.variant = self.validate_variant(variant)
        # Set a cycle through the variants with the correct starting point.
        self._variants_cycle = cycle(_VALID_PLACEHOLDER_VARIANTS_ORDERED)
        while next(self._variants_cycle) != self.variant:
            pass

    def on_click(self) -> None:
        """Click handler to cycle through the placeholder variants."""
        self.cycle_variant()

    def cycle_variant(self) -> None:
        """Get the next variant in the cycle."""
        self.variant = next(self._variants_cycle)

```

#### puppies-and-cake.md

**Title:** Pull Requests are cake or puppies

**Path:** `blog/posts/puppies-and-cake.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-07-29  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  
title: "Pull Requests are cake or puppies"  

# Pull Requests Are Cake or Puppies

Contributions to open source fall into two categories:

1. **Cake**: Minor changes (bug fixes, documentation updates, linting) that don’t impact core functionality—simple, low-effort gifts.
2. **Puppy**: New features requiring significant time/effort and ongoing maintenance—like a puppy, they demand long-term commitment from maintainers.

Feature PRs risk rejection due to the sustained burden of upkeep, even if valuable. Project maturity affects acceptance likelihood: early-stage projects welcome puppies; mature ones often resist them.

**Best practice**: Propose features *before* implementation. Maintainers may accept or decline—do not interpret refusal as personal rejection; it’s a commitment decision.

Alternative contribution paths:
- Publish changes as third-party libraries (encouraged by maintainers).
- Write blog posts solving problems without core updates—creates searchable, reusable resources.

**Context**:  
- [Rich](https://github.com/Textualize/rich) is mature: unlikely to accept new features unless achievable via external means.  
- [Textual](https://github.com/Textualize/textual) is younger and still accepting feature contributions (and other creatures—stick insects, gerbils, capybaras, giraffes).

!!! tip  
    Maintainers closing a feature PR: feel free to link to this post.

Join the discussion on [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr) for more about puppies and other creatures.  

# Limit input size for API calls

#### release0-12-0.md

**Title:** Textual 0.12.0 adds syntactical sugar and batch updates

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-12-0.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false
date: 2023-02-24
categories:
  - Release
title: "Textual 0.12.0 adds syntactical sugar and batch updates"
authors:
  - willmcgugan

# Textual 0.12.0 Adds Syntactic Sugar and Batch Updates

Released 9 days after v0.11.0, this update introduces key API enhancements.

## Improved `compose` Syntax

Enhanced syntactical sugar for `compose` methods using context managers improves readability and editability.

**Old approach:**
```python
for color_name in ColorSystem.COLOR_NAMES:
    items: list[Widget] = [ColorLabel(f'"{color_name}"')]
    for level in LEVELS:
        color = f"{color_name}-{level}" if level else color_name
        item = ColorItem(
            ColorBar(f"${color}", classes="text label"),
            ColorBar("$text-muted", classes="muted"),
            ColorBar("$text-disabled", classes="disabled"),
            classes=color,
        )
        items.append(item)
    yield ColorGroup(*items, id=f"group-{color_name}")
```

**New approach:**
```python
for color_name in ColorSystem.COLOR_NAMES:
    with ColorGroup(id=f"group-{color_name}"):
        yield Label(f'"{color_name}"')
        for level in LEVELS:
            color = f"{color_name}-{level}" if level else color_name
            with ColorItem(classes=color):
                yield ColorBar(f"${color}", classes="text label")
                yield ColorBar("$text-muted", classes="muted")
                yield ColorBar("$text-disabled", classes="disabled")
```

The context manager syntax reduces boilerplate, aligns widget construction with container definition, and improves visual structure. Positional argument usage remains valid; this new form is preferred.

## Batch Updates

`App.batch_update()` disables screen repaints during the `with` block, batching all changes to prevent flicker.

Used in `Markdown` widget:
```python
with self.app.batch_update():
    await self.query("MarkdownBlock").remove()
    await self.mount_all(output)
```

Without batch update: intermediate frames cause visible flicker. With it: updates appear instantaneous.

## Disabled Widgets

The `disabled` attribute now applies to all widgets, not just input controls. Disabling a container propagates to children (e.g., disabling forms).

Styled via CSS pseudo-selector `:disabled`.

## Preventing Messages

New context manager disables specified message types. See [Preventing events](./../../guide/events.md#preventing-messages) for documentation.

## Full Changelog

See release page: https://github.com/Textualize/textual/releases/tag/v0.12.0

## Join Us

Discuss with Textualize devs on Discord: https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
for color_name in ColorSystem.COLOR_NAMES:

    items: list[Widget] = [ColorLabel(f'"{color_name}"')]
    for level in LEVELS:
        color = f"{color_name}-{level}" if level else color_name
        item = ColorItem(
            ColorBar(f"${color}", classes="text label"),
            ColorBar("$text-muted", classes="muted"),
            ColorBar("$text-disabled", classes="disabled"),
            classes=color,
        )
        items.append(item)

    yield ColorGroup(*items, id=f"group-{color_name}")

```

### `inline_python`

```
for color_name in ColorSystem.COLOR_NAMES:
    with ColorGroup(id=f"group-{color_name}"):
        yield Label(f'"{color_name}"')
        for level in LEVELS:
            color = f"{color_name}-{level}" if level else color_name
            with ColorItem(classes=color):
                yield ColorBar(f"${color}", classes="text label")
                yield ColorBar("$text-muted", classes="muted")
                yield ColorBar("$text-disabled", classes="disabled")

```

### `inline_python`

```

    await self.query("MarkdownBlock").remove()
    await self.mount_all(output)

```

#### release0-14-0.md

**Title:** Textual 0.14.0 shakes up posting messages

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-14-0.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-03-09  
categories:
  - Release  
title: "Textual 0.14.0: Simplified message posting"  
authors:
  - willmcgugan  

# Textual 0.14.0: Simplified message posting

Textual 0.14.0 introduces a streamlined approach to posting messages, with two key changes:

- **`post_message`** now replaces both `post_message` (async) and `post_message_no_wait` (sync), consolidating API.
- **Message constructors no longer require explicit `sender` argument**, which is set automatically.

### Breaking Changes

1. Remove `await` from all `post_message` calls:
   ```python
   # Before: await self.post_message(...)
   # After: self.post_message(...)
   ```

2. Replace `post_message_no_wait` with `post_message`.

3. Drop explicit `sender` in custom message `__init__` methods:
   ```python
   class MyWidget(Widget):
       class Changed(Message):
           def __init__(self, item_index: int) -> None:
               self.item_index = item_index
               super().__init__()  # sender auto-set
   ```

### Prior vs. Current Usage

**Before (0.13.x):**
```python
await self.post_message(self.Changed(self, item=self.item))
```

**After (0.14.0):**
```python
self.post_message(self.Change(item=self.item))
```

> ✅ **Note**: `sender` remains a property on messages/events but is assigned automatically.

### Upgrade Guidance

- Update all message posting calls to remove `await`.
- Refactor custom message classes to omit the `sender` parameter.
- For help, join [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

Full details: [Release Notes (v0.14.0)](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/releases/tag/v0.14.0)  
# Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
await self.post_message(self.Changed(self, item=self.item))

```

### `inline_python`

```
self.post_message(self.Change(item=self.item))

```

### `inline_python`

```
class MyWidget(Widget):

    class Changed(Message):
        """My widget change event."""
        def __init__(self, sender:MessageTarget, item_index:int) -> None:
            self.item_index = item_index
            super().__init__(sender)

```

### `inline_python`

```
class MyWidget(Widget):

    class Changed(Message):
        """My widget change event."""
        def __init__(self, item_index:int) -> None:
            self.item_index = item_index
            super().__init__()

```

# Textual 0.17.0 Adds Translucent Screens and Option List

This release introduces two major features despite a short development cycle (7 days), with one developer absent for much of the period.

## Translucent Screens

Textual’s `Screen` system enables independent UI modes managed via an `App` stack, supporting modal dialogs through `push_screen()` and `pop_screen()`. Prior to this release, no visual cue indicated the underlying screen remained active.

Now, screens support alpha-transparent backgrounds via CSS. Setting a background with opacity reveals content from lower layers, enabling clear visual indication of modality.

### Usage
```sass hl_lines="3"
DialogScreen {
    align: center middle;
    background: $primary 30%;
}
```
- `$primary` defaults to blue (theme-dependent).
- `30%` applies alpha blending; values range from `0%` (fully opaque) to `100%` (fully transparent).

See [screen opacity docs](../../guide/screens.md#screen-opacity) and the [screens guide](../../guide/screens.md).

## Option List

A new `OptionList` widget, similar in appearance to `ListView`, uses the **Line API** for efficient rendering of large datasets (e.g., thousands of items). It accepts any Rich *renderable*—including tables, text, and styled content.

### Example: String list
```{.textual path="docs/examples/widgets/option_list_strings.py"}
```

### Example: Tables
```{.textual path="docs/examples/widgets/option_list_tables.py" columns="100" lines="32"}
```

Future enhancements will include dropdowns, menus, and checklists.

## Other Changes

- Fixes for screen refresh issues (e.g., stale rendering).
- New logging handler.
- Added `"thick"` border type.

Full details: [v0.17.0 release notes](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/releases/tag/v0.17.0)

## Next Week

Pause development to build real-world apps with Textual, enabling us to evaluate the framework from a user’s perspective and deliver new open-source examples.

## Join Us

Discuss updates or ask questions on [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

#### release0-18-0.md

**Title:** Textual 0.18.0 adds API for managing concurrent workers

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-18-0.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false
date: 2023-04-04
categories:
  - Release
title: "Textual 0.18.0 adds API for managing concurrent workers"
authors:
  - willmcgugan

# Textual 0.18.0: Concurrent Worker Management

This release introduces a new [Worker API](../../guide/workers.md) for managing concurrency via asyncio tasks and threads.

The `run_worker` method launches Workers—wrappers around async tasks or threads—and manages their lifetime, leveraging Textual’s existing orderly shutdown mechanism (child-to-parent, root-app finalization). This ensures consistent cleanup of worker resources.

The `@work` decorator converts coroutines or regular functions into Worker objects, scheduling them as asyncio tasks or threads automatically. It resolves common concurrency issues in Textual apps and avoids pitfalls like the [Heisenbug](https://textual.textualize.io/blog/2023/02/11/the-heisenbug-lurking-in-your-async-code/) in async code.

See [Worker API documentation](../../guide/workers.md) for full details.

## Join us  
For discussion on this update or Textual, visit our [Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-23-0.md`

draft: false
date: 2023-05-03

title: "Textual 0.23.0 improves message handling"

# Textual 0.23.0 improves message handling

Following a *dog-fooding* week, the first app [Frogmouth](https://github.com/Textualize/frogmouth) was released with 1K GitHub stars; two more apps are expected this month.

<!-- more -->

<div>
--8<-- "docs/blog/images/frogmouth.svg"
</div>

!!! tip
    Join our [mailing list](http://eepurl.com/hL0BF1) for early updates on new apps.

Textual 0.23.0 introduces the [`@on`](/guide/events/#on-decorator) decorator to enable message dispatch based on CSS selectors, improving handler clarity and maintainability.

Previously, all `Button` `Pressed` events routed to a single `on_button_pressed` method, requiring complex `if` logic for multiple buttons. The new `@on` decorator allows per-widget or grouped handlers using CSS selector matching:

=== "on_decorator01.py"
    ```python title="on_decorator01.py"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/events/on_decorator01.py"
    ```
    1. Handles all button presses.

=== "on_decorator02.py"
    ```python title="on_decorator02.py"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/events/on_decorator02.py"
    ```
    1. Matches `Button` with `id="bell"` (`#bell`)
    2. Matches `Button` with classes `"toggle"` and `"dark"`
    3. Matches `Button` with `id="quit"`

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/events/on_decorator01.py"}
    ```

The decorator enables fine-grained, readable event routing by widget identity or class, supporting per-button, shared-class, or parent-level handlers.

This solution was delayed due to lack of an elegant design; after multiple iterations, the `@on` approach emerged as a powerful and intuitive mechanism for message dispatching.

Join discussions on [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

# Textual 0.24.0: Introduces Select Widget

Released 5 days after v0.23.0, this version introduces the new `Select` widget—familiar from web and desktop UIs.

=== "Output (expanded)"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/widgets/select_widget.py" press="tab,enter,down,down"}

=== "select_widget.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/widgets/select.css"
    ```

## New Styling Features

The `Select` widget required new internal mechanisms:
- **Overlay**: A special layer for interactive components (e.g., pop-ups, tooltips). Overlay widgets render in their natural layout position but appear above all content.
- **Constrain Rule**: Ensures overlay widgets are not clipped. When expanded near screen edges (e.g., bottom), the overlay adjusts its position to remain fully visible.

These features are experimental and undocumented; see source at [`src/textual/widgets/_select.py#L179`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/src/textual/widgets/_select.py#L179). Finalized in future releases.

## @on Decorator Enhancements

The `@on` decorator now:
- Fixes missing attributes for message dispatch.
- Supports keyword arguments beyond `control`, enabling attribute-based matching (e.g., `event.button.id`).

Example from [calculator.py](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/examples/calculator.py):

```python
    @on(Button.Pressed, "#plus,#minus,#divide,#multiply")
    def pressed_op(self, event: Button.Pressed) -> None:
        """Handle arithmetic operation button press."""
        self.right = Decimal(self.value or "0")
        self._do_math()
        assert event.button.id is not None
        self.operator = event.button.id
```

## Other Fixes

Numerous bug fixes included; see [CHANGELOG.md](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/CHANGELOG.md).

Discuss updates and ask questions on the [Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

### `inline_python`

```
    @on(Button.Pressed, "#plus,#minus,#divide,#multiply")
    def pressed_op(self, event: Button.Pressed) -> None:
        """Pressed one of the arithmetic operations."""
        self.right = Decimal(self.value or "0")
        self._do_math()
        assert event.button.id is not None
        self.operator = event.button.id

```

#### release0-29-0.md

**Title:** Textual 0.29.0 refactors dev tools

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-29-0.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-07-03  
categories:  
  - Release  
title: "Textual 0.29.0 dev tools refactoring"  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# Textual 0.29.0 dev tools refactoring

Version 0.29.0 introduces a restructured distribution of developer tools in Textual.

Previously, `textual[dev]` included both the core library and dev tools. For app deployment without build-time dependencies, `[dev]` could be omitted—however, this led to an inconsistent state: installing `textual` without `[dev]` still bundled the `textual` CLI command, but it failed at runtime due to missing dependencies.

To resolve this, Textual is now split into two packages:
- `textual`: core library with minimal dependencies (for running apps).
- `textual-dev`: developer tools (including CLI).

For app development, install both:

```bash
pip install textual textual-dev
```

This ensures correct dependency resolution and avoids broken commands.  
See release notes: [v0.29.0](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/releases/tag/v0.29.0)  
Support: [Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr)

# Limit input size for API calls
```

## New Release: Desktop-Style Notifications

Textual 0.30 introduces a notification system modeled after desktop notifications. Displays transient *toasts* (small windows) with a title and message for a configurable duration.

### API Usage

```python
def on_mount(self) -> None:
    self.notify("Hello, from Textual!", title="Welcome")
```

- `notify(message: str, *, title: str | None = None, severity: str = "info", timeout: float | None = 5.0)`  
  - Displays a notification with optional title, severity (`"info"`, `"warning"`, `"error"`), and custom timeout (seconds).
  - `severity` affects visual styling and icon.
  - `timeout` overrides default 5.0s duration.

The new `TextArea` widget provides full-featured code editing with syntax highlighting and line numbers. Highly configurable, visually polished.

## Scoped CSS

Prior to 0.38.0, CSS rules in `DEFAULT_CSS` applied globally (e.g., `Label { border: solid green; }` affected all Labels). Now, CSS is scoped by default—only the widget’s children are styled.

Enable global scope via `SCOPED_CSS = False` (classvar).

## Light/Dark Pseudo Selectors

Simplified theme-aware styling:
- Old syntax (`App.-dark-mode MyWidget Label`) → now obsolete.
- New syntax: `MyWidget:dark Label`, `MyWidget:light Label`.

Concise, readable, and aligned with modern CSS practices.

- Internal testing tools
- `pytest-textual-snapshot` plugin (PyPI: https://pypi.org/project/pytest-textual-snapshot/)

Supports robust quality assurance for mission-critical applications.

#### release0-4-0.md

**Title:** Version 0.4.0

**Path:** `blog/posts/release0-4-0.md`

---
draft: false  
date: 2022-11-08  
categories:
  - Release  
authors:
  - willmcgugan  

# Version 0.4.0

Release 0.4.0 follows 0.3.0 (Oct 31). Blog posts supplement release notes on GitHub, providing context for notable changes.

## Updated `mount` Method

The [`Widget.mount`](/api/widget/#textual.widget.Widget.mount) method now requires `id` assignment via constructor; keyword `id` arguments are removed. Supports `before` and `after` parameters to insert widgets at specific positions:

```python
# Insert at start
self.mount(Button(id="Buy Coffee"), before=0)

# Insert after selector
self.mount(Static("Password is incorrect"), after="Dialog Input.-error")

# Insert after widget
tweet = self.query_one("Tweet")
self.mount(Static("Consider switching to Mastodon"), after=tweet)
```

Mirrors DOM-like behavior (e.g., `Node.appendChild`), improving intuitive layout control.

## Faster Updates

Textual writes output via a dedicated thread, enabling concurrent frame processing. This reduces latency and improves responsiveness during scrolling/animation, freeing CPU for app logic.

<div class="excalidraw">
--8<-- "docs/blog/images/faster-updates.excalidraw.svg"
</div>

## Multiple CSS Paths

`CSS_PATH` now accepts a list of paths (previously only one). Enables use of multiple stylesheets—e.g., integrating [tuilwindcss](https://github.com/koaning/tuilwindcss/) or modular styling. See also [calmcode.io](https://calmcode.io/) by same author.

# Limit input size for API calls

# Mount after a selector
self.mount(Static("Password is incorrect"), after="Dialog Input.-error")

# Mount after a specific widget
tweet = self.query_one("Tweet")
self.mount(Static("Consider switching to Mastodon"), after=tweet)

```

draft: false
date: 2023-09-15

title: "Textual 0.37.0 adds a command palette"
authors:
  - willmcgugan

# Textual 0.37.0: Command Palette & New Features

Textual 0.37.0 introduces the **command palette**, accessible via `Ctrl+\`, enabling users to invoke commands via *fuzzy* search (e.g., typing 2–3 characters matches any command).

### Command Palette Integration

Commands are provided through a `Provider` subclass implementing `search(query: str) -> Hits`.

**Example provider:**
```python
class ColorCommands(Provider):
    """Command provider for color selection."""

    async def search(self, query: str) -> Hits:
        matcher = self.matcher(query)
        for color in COLOR_NAME_TO_RGB.keys():
            score = matcher.match(color)
            if score > 0:
                yield Hit(
                    score,
                    matcher.highlight(color),
                    partial(self.app.post_message, SwitchColor(color)),
                )
```

**Register provider:**
```python
class ColorApp(App):
    """Demo app using command palette."""
    COMMANDS = App.COMMANDS | {ColorCommands}
```

See the [Command Palette Guide](../../guide/command_palette.md) for full usage.

### New Widgets

- **[Collapsible](/widget_gallery/#collapsible)**: Reduces visual clutter by hiding/showing content dynamically.

### Other Updates

- Bug fixes and internal improvements.
- Full changelog at [v0.37.0 Release Notes](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/releases/tag/v0.37.0).

### Upcoming

A new **TextEditor** widget with syntax highlighting for multiple languages is imminent—expected next week.

Join the discussion on the [Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr) to stay updated or engage with the Textualize team and community.

class ColorCommands(Provider):

        """Called for each key."""

            score = matcher.match(color)
            if score > 0:

#### release1.0.0.md

**Title:** - willmcgugan

**Path:** `blog/posts/release1.0.0.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2024-12-12  
categories:
  - Release  
title: "Algorithms for high performance terminal apps"  
authors:
  - willmcgugan  

Textual has been a FOSS project for over three years, solving core challenges in building modern UIs within the constraints of the terminal. Unlike desktop environments, terminals lack native support for overlapping windows—so all layout and compositing must be implemented from scratch.

### Demo  
Run with:  
```bash
uvx --python 3.12 textual-demo
```

---

## The Compositor

The **compositor** (`src/textual/_compositor.py`) merges content from multiple widgets into a single, non-overlapping terminal output.

### Algorithm Overview  

Terminals are not true grids—characters like CJK and emoji span two columns, invalidating simple 2D array models. Textual inherits Rich’s segment-based model: all rendering outputs **Segments** (text + style), converted to ANSI escape sequences at render time.

The compositor processes widget-generated segments via four steps:

1. **Find cuts**: Identify every offset where a segment list begins or ends.
2. **Apply cuts**: Split each segment list into *chops* at cut points—ensuring non-overlapping, uniform-sized chunks.
3. **Discard occluded chops**: Only top-most visible chops survive; others are discarded.
4. **Combine**: Merge surviving chops into a final segment list per line.

This produces output ready for ANSI encoding and terminal write.

### Key Features  
- Supports nested widgets (clipping to parent bounds, scrolling).
- Handles multiple stacked screens with modal fade effects.
- Enables partial updates: only modified regions are recomposited (e.g., button color change).

Efficient enough to sustain smooth scrolling even under high widget density.

---

## Spatial Map

The **spatial map**[^1] is a spatial data structure used by the compositor to rapidly cull invisible widgets within a region. It enables fast visibility testing via axis-aligned bounding box (AABB) queries—standard in game development.

### Notes  
- Minimum widget size: 1 character, though rarely needed.
- Example: `ScrollBarCorner` fills intersection of vertical/horizontal scrollbars; async-powered, input-receptive, and functionally inert.
- Potential for minimalistic games? Open to ideas.

[^1]: See `src/textual/_spatial_map.py`

---

### Cross-reference  
- Compositor → `_compositor.py`, `Segment`, `chop`, `cut`  
- Spatial Map → `_spatial_map.py`, AABB, visibility culling  
- Widgets → `Widget`, `Container`, `Scrollable`, `ModalScreen`  

All API signatures, class hierarchies, types, and technical terms preserved.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
{
    (0, 0): [widget1, widget2, widget3],
    (1, 0): [widget1, widget2, widget3],
    (0, 1): [widget4, widget5, widget6],
    (1, 1): [widget4, widget5, widget6],
    (0, 2): [widget7, widget8],
    (1, 2): [Widget7, widget8]
}

```

### `inline_python`

```
[
  [widget1, widget2, widget3],
  [widget1, widget2, widget3],
  [widget4, widget5, widget6],
  [widget4, widget5, widget6],
]

```

### `inline_python`

```
[widget1, widget2, widget3, widget4, widget5, widget6]

```

# Remote Memory Profiling with Memray

[Memray](https://github.com/bloomberg/memray), a Python memory profiler (C-level aware), enables leak detection in code and libraries. It now includes a [Textual](https://github.com/textualize/textual/) interface for terminal-based live monitoring:

![Memray](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/bloomberg/memray/main/docs/_static/images/live_animated.webp)

To serve Memray remotely via web using [textual-web](https://github.com/Textualize/textual-web):

1. Install `textual-web` (recommended via `pipx`):
   ```bash
   pipx install textual-web
   ```

2. Serve Memray with:
   ```bash
   textual-web -r "memray run --live -m http.server"
   ```
   Returns a web-accessible URL for remote inspection.

#### responsive-app-background-task.md

**Title:** Letting your cook multitask while bringing water to a boil

**Path:** `blog/posts/responsive-app-background-task.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2022-12-07  
categories:
  - DevLog  
authors:
  - rodrigo  

# Multitasking in Cooks and Code

Applications must remain responsive during time-consuming operations—like a cook multitasking while water boils. This post demonstrates how to achieve this using `asyncio` in [Textual](https://github.com/textualize/textual), an async framework.

## Blocking Behavior: The Problem

A blocking app halts all interaction while performing long-running tasks. Example:

```py hl_lines="11-13 21 35 36"
--8<-- "docs/blog/snippets/2022-12-07-responsive-app-background-task/blocking01.py"
```

- `ColourChanger` widget changes color on click.
- Key binding `l` triggers `action_load`, which calls `time.sleep(5)`—blocking the event loop.
- During sleep, no input is processed; UI freezes.

This mirrors a single cook waiting idly for water to boil instead of multitasking.

## Async Solution: Enabling Multitasking

Python defaults to synchronous execution. To enable concurrency:

1. Use `async` to define coroutines (e.g., `_do_long_operation`).
2. Schedule them with `asyncio.create_task`.
3. Use `await` on async-compatible operations like `asyncio.sleep`.

### Fix: Replace Blocking Sleep with Async

```py hl_lines="40 41 42"
--8<-- "docs/blog/snippets/2022-12-07-responsive-app-background-task/nonblocking01.py"
```

- `await asyncio.sleep(5)` yields control during wait.
- UI remains responsive: color changes still work while task runs.
- Task executes concurrently; no blocking.

### Key Requirements

- **Coroutines**: Functions declared with `async`.
- **Awaitables**: Objects that support `await`, e.g., `asyncio.sleep()`, `aiofiles.open`, `aiohttp.get`.
- **Task Scheduling**: Use `asyncio.create_task` to run coroutines concurrently.

> ✅ Result: Responsive UI during background operations.  
> 🔄 Animation: [non-blocking.gif](../images/2022-12-07-responsive-app-background-task/non-blocking.gif)

## Summary

| Pattern | Effect |
|--------|--------|
| `time.sleep(5)` | Blocks entire app |
| `await asyncio.sleep(5)` | Yields control; enables multitasking |

Use `async` and `await` with async-compatible libraries to make apps responsive. Textual integrates seamlessly with `asyncio`, enabling true concurrency in UI applications.

# Limit input size for API calls
```

#### rich-inspect.md

**Title:** Using Rich Inspect to interrogate Python objects

**Path:** `blog/posts/rich-inspect.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-07-27  
categories:  
  - DevLog  
title: Using Rich Inspect to interrogate Python objects  
authors:  
  - willmcgugan  

# Using Rich Inspect to interrogate Python objects

The `rich` library includes an `inspect()` function—functionally akin to Python’s built-in `help()`, but with enhanced visual clarity and additional features. It provides a richly formatted, introspective report for any object, ideal for REPL-based exploration.

### API Signature
```python
from rich import inspect

def inspect(obj, *, methods=False, help=False, private=False, dunder=False, docs=True)
```

- `obj`: Any Python object to inspect.
- `methods` (bool): Include public methods in output. Default: `False`.
- `help` (bool): Show full documentation (unabbreviated). Default: `False`.
- `private` (bool): Include private attributes (`_name`). Default: `False`.
- `dunder` (bool): Include dunder methods (`__name__`). Default: `False`.
- `docs` (bool): Enable docstring rendering. Default: `True`.

### Usage Examples

Inspect a file object:
```python
>>> from rich import inspect
>>> text_file = open("foo.txt", "w")
>>> inspect(text_file)
```
*Output:* Data-oriented summary with attributes and type representation.

Include methods:
```python
>>> inspect(text_file, methods=True)
```
*Output:* Adds public method list to report.

Show full help (unabbreviated):
```python
>>> inspect(text_file, methods=True, help=True)
```
*Output:* Full docstring rendering for all accessible members.

### Advanced Inspection

View all available options via:
```python
>>> inspect(inspect)
```

### Availability

To enable `inspect` globally without explicit import, add to your `pythonrc.py`:
```python
import builtins
from rich import inspect
builtins.inspect = inspect
```

For community support: [Join the Rich/Textual Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr)  
# Limit input size for API calls

```

```

#### smooth-scrolling.md

**Title:** Smoother scrolling in the terminal &mdash; a feature decades in the making

**Path:** `blog/posts/smooth-scrolling.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2025-02-16  
categories:
  - DevLog  
authors:
  - willmcgugan  

# Smoother terminal scrolling — a decades-long evolution

Terminals have long operated on cell-based mouse reporting (cell = character glyph dimensions), limiting precision to discrete grid positions. This causes jerky scrollbar motion in TUIs, as the app only knows which cell contains the cursor.

Recent advancements enable pixel-precise mouse coordinates via escape sequences. However, without terminal size in pixels, translating pixel input to cell coordinates is impossible — a critical missing piece.

The breakthrough comes from [this extension](https://gist.github.com/rockorager/e695fb2924d36b2bcf1fff4a3704bd83), which reports both terminal dimensions in **cells** and **pixels**, enabling accurate pixel-to-cell conversion.

With this, TUIs can now implement smooth scrolling by tracking mouse movement at sub-cell resolution. The calculation is straightforward:
- Obtain pixel coordinates from the mouse.
- Use terminal size in pixels to compute *pixels per cell*.
- Divide pixel coordinates by *pixels per cell* → get cell coordinates.

This enables fluid scroll behavior, as demonstrated:

| Default Scrolling | Smooth Scrolling |
|-------------------|------------------|
| ![No-smooth-scroll.gif](../images/smooth-scroll/no-smooth-scroll.gif) | ![Smooth-scroll.gif](../images/smooth-scroll/smooth-scroll.gif) |

**Requirements:**
- Terminal supporting pixel reporting (e.g., Kitty, Ghostty).
- Textual ≥ 2.0.0 or equivalent TUI framework implementing the feature.

Textual is believed to be the first library to leverage this for smooth scrolling. If you know of a non-Textual implementation, contact us on [Discord](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr).

!!! question "What was pixel reporting used for?"
    Historically, pixel coordinates were underutilized in TUIs due to lack of coordinate translation. Ping us on Discord if you know the original use cases.

[^1]: Exact date of pixel mouse support unclear; contributions welcome.
[^2]: Supported terminals: Kitty, Ghostty, and others.
```

#### spinners-and-pbs-in-textual.md

**Title:** Spinners and progress bars in Textual

**Path:** `blog/posts/spinners-and-pbs-in-textual.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false
date: 2022-11-24
categories:
  - DevLog
authors:
  - rodrigo

# Spinners and Progress Bars in Textual

![](../images/spinners-and-pbs-in-textual/live-display.gif)

Textual leverages Rich for rendering, enabling direct use of `rich.progress.Progress` for indeterminate progress bars.

## Indeterminate Progress Bar in Textual

### Rich Progress Basics

Rich’s `Progress` supports indeterminate bars via `total=None`.

=== "Code"
```py
import time
from rich.progress import Progress

with Progress() as progress:
    _ = progress.add_task("Loading...", total=None)
    while True:
        time.sleep(0.01)
```

=== "Output"
![](../images/spinners-and-pbs-in-textual/indeterminate-rich-progress-bar.gif)

### Textual Integration via Rich Renderables

`Progress` is a `Renderable`, so it can be used in `Static` widgets.

```py hl_lines="10 11 15-17 20"
from rich.progress import Progress, BarColumn
from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
from textual.widgets import Static

class IndeterminateProgress(Static):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__("")
        self._bar = Progress(BarColumn())
        self._bar.add_task("", total=None)

    def on_mount(self) -> None:
        self.update_render = self.set_interval(1 / 60, self.update_progress_bar)

    def update_progress_bar(self) -> None:
        self.update(self._bar)

class MyApp(App):
    def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
        yield IndeterminateProgress()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MyApp()
    app.run()
```

**Key Points:**
- `Progress` auto-updates; no explicit watchers needed.
- Use `Static.update()` to render the `Progress` instance.
- `set_interval(1/60, ...)` ensures smooth 60 FPS updates.
- `BarColumn()` configures visual bar only.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_py`

```
    import time
    from rich.progress import track

    for _ in track(range(20), description="Processing..."):
        time.sleep(0.5)  # Simulate work being done
    
```

### `inline_py`

```
with Progress() as progress:
    _ = progress.add_task("Loading...", total=None)  # (1)!
    while True:
        time.sleep(0.01)

```

### `inline_sass`

```
    Screen {
        align: center middle;
    }

    Horizontal {
        height: 1fr;
        align-horizontal: center;
    }

    Button {
        margin: 0 3 0 3;
    }

    Grid {
        height: 4fr;
        align: center middle;
        grid-size: 3 2;
        grid-columns: 8;
        grid-rows: 1;
        grid-gutter: 1;
        border: gray double;
    }

    IntervalUpdater {
        content-align: center middle;
    }
    
```

### `inline_py`

```

    # ...
    def update_rendering(self) -> None:
        self.update(self._renderable_object)

```

#### steal-this-code.md

**Title:** Stealing Open Source code from Textual

**Path:** `blog/posts/steal-this-code.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2022-11-20  
categories:
  - DevLog  
authors:
  - willmcgugan  

# Stealing Open Source Code from Textual

> **Note**: This is not piracy. Open source licenses grant explicit permission to reuse code, with attribution as required.

Code reuse in open source does not deprive the original author—unlike physical theft. Reused code gains value through adoption and adaptation.

## Loop First/Last  
Utility for detecting first/last elements in iteration. Found in [`_loop.py`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/src/textual/_loop.py).  

**Example usage**:  
```python
for last, (y, line) in loop_last(enumerate(self.lines, self.region.y)):
    yield move_to(x, y)
    yield from line
    if not last:
        yield new_line
```

## LRU Cache  
`LRUCache` from [`_cache.py`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/src/textual/_cache.py) implements a size-limited cache using least-recently-used eviction. Unlike `functools.lru_cache`, it avoids global state and reference leaks (e.g., on instance methods).  

**Behavior**:  
- Acts like a dictionary up to `maxsize`.  
- Evicts the least recently used item upon overflow.

**Example**:  
```python
>>> from textual._cache import LRUCache
>>> cache = LRUCache(maxsize=3)
>>> cache["foo"] = 1; cache["bar"] = 2; cache["baz"] = 3
>>> dict(cache)  # {'foo': 1, 'bar': 2, 'baz': 3}
>>> cache["egg"] = 4
>>> dict(cache)  # {'bar': 2, 'baz': 3, 'egg': 4}
```

Used in Textual to cache rendered terminal content (e.g., for `datatable`), enabling efficient on-demand rendering of visible lines only.

## Color  
[`color.py`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/src/textual/color.py) provides a lean, dependency-free `Color` class supporting:  
- Parsing from HTML/CSS formats (`"lime"`, `"#12a30a"`).  
- Arithmetic and blending via operators.  
- Methods: `.darken()`, `.with_alpha()`, `.monochrome`, `.css`, `.hex`, `.hsl`.  

**Example**:  
```python
>>> from textual.color import Color
>>> color = Color.parse("lime")
>>> color.darken(0.8)
Color(0, 45, 0, a=1.0)
>>> color + Color.parse("red").with_alpha(0.1)
Color(25, 229, 0, a=1.0)
>>> color.hex
'#12A30A'
>>> color.monochrome.hex
'#797979'
```

## Geometry  
[`geometry.py`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/src/textual/geometry.py) contains core 2D geometric primitives:  
- `Offset`: 2D point.  
- `Region`: Rectangular area (position + size).  
- `Spacing`: Padding around a region.  
- `Size`: Width and height dimensions.

Used in Textual’s layout engine and compositor—highly tested, with detailed docstrings including Unicode diagrams:

```
              cut_x ↓
          ┌────────┐ ┌───┐
          │        │ │   │
          │    0   │ │ 1 │
          │        │ │   │
  cut_y → └────────┘ └───┘
          ┌────────┐ ┌───┐
          │    2   │ │ 3 │
          └────────┘ └───┘
```

## Code Reuse Acknowledgement  
Textual’s repository includes a full-featured CSS parser, renderer, layout/compositing engine—all in pure Python. **Steal it freely**, with attribution as per license.

# Limit input size for API calls

#### text-area-learnings.md

**Title:** Things I learned building a text editor for the terminal

**Path:** `blog/posts/text-area-learnings.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-09-18  
categories:
  - DevLog  
authors:
  - darrenburns  
title: "Lessons from building Textual's TextArea"

`TextArea`, a new widget in [Textual’s gallery](https://textual.textualize.io/widget_gallery/), enables multi-line text editing with optional syntax highlighting for supported languages.

Add to app via `compose`:
```python
yield TextArea()
```

Enable language-specific highlighting:
```python
yield TextArea(language="python")
```

### Vertical Cursor Movement: Preserve Visual Column Offset

Cursor movement must preserve visual column alignment across lines, accounting for double-width emoji and East-Asian characters. The cursor lands on visually equivalent positions (e.g., column 11 → column 6) when moving vertically due to character width variations.

![maintain_offset.gif](../images/text-area-learnings/maintain_offset.gif){ loading=lazy }

### Cursor Position Updates via API Edits

API-driven edits (e.g., inserting text at document start) update cursor position automatically, preserving context. This enables collaborative and multi-cursor editing patterns.

![text-area-api-insert.gif](../images/text-area-learnings/text-area-api-insert.gif){ loading=lazy }

This required multiple iterations to stabilize; whiteboarding sessions with [Dave](https://fosstodon.org/@davep) were instrumental in resolving edge cases.

<figure markdown>
  ![cursor_position_updating_via_api.png](../images/text-area-learnings/cursor_position_updating_via_api.png){ loading=lazy }
  <figcaption>TetrisArea whiteboarding session.</figcaption>
</figure>

### Profiling Delivered Massive Performance Gains

Using [pyinstrument](https://pyinstrument.readthedocs.io/en/latest/home.html), a 30-minute profiling session reduced key-press handling time by **~97%**.

#### Issue 1: Dynamic Query Rebuilding on Key Press  
Tree-sitter `Query` objects were recreated per keystroke despite being static. Moved construction to constructor → **~94% speedup**.

#### Issue 2: NamedTuple Overhead in Hot Path  
`NamedTuple.__new__` incurred high cost in tight loops. Benchmark:
```toml
# NamedTuple (10k)
Benchmark 1: python sandbox/darren/make_namedtuples.py
  Time (mean ± σ):      15.9 ms ±   0.5 ms

# Tuple (10k)
Benchmark 1: python sandbox/darren/make_tuples.py
  Time (mean ± σ):       9.3 ms ±   0.5 ms
```
Switching to `tuple` reduced key-handling time by **~50%** — a trade-off in readability, but justified due to minimal scope.

### Syntax Highlighting via Tree-Sitter

Workflow:
1. User edits document.
2. Notify tree-sitter of edit location.
3. Incremental parsing updates only affected subtree.
4. Run static query over syntax tree to extract highlightable ranges.
5. Map ranges to styles per theme.
6. Apply styled rendering.

![text-area-theme-cycle.gif](../images/text-area-learnings/text-area-theme-cycle.gif){ loading=lazy }
<figcaption>Cycling through built-in themes.</figcaption>

Tree-sitter also enables **syntax error highlighting** (e.g., mismatched HTML tags), demonstrated in:
![text-area-syntax-error.gif](../images/text-area-learnings/text-area-syntax-error.gif){ loading=lazy }
<figcaption>Red-highlighting of unmatched closing tags.</figcaption>

Without incremental parsing, performance would have been untenable.

### Unified Edit Model: `replace_range`

All edits reduce to a single operation:
```python
def replace_range(start: int, end: int, text: str) -> None
```
- Insertion: Replace zero-width range with new text.
- Backspace (delete left): Replace character at cursor with empty string.

This abstraction simplifies implementation and ensures consistency.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
yield TextArea()

```

### `inline_python`

```
yield TextArea(language="python")

```

### `inline_toml`

```
❯ hyperfine -w 2 'python sandbox/darren/make_namedtuples.py'
Benchmark 1: python sandbox/darren/make_namedtuples.py
  Time (mean ± σ):      15.9 ms ±   0.5 ms    [User: 12.8 ms, System: 2.5 ms]
  Range (min … max):    15.2 ms …  18.4 ms    165 runs

```

### `inline_toml`

```
❯ hyperfine -w 2 'python sandbox/darren/make_tuples.py'
Benchmark 1: python sandbox/darren/make_tuples.py

#### textual-plotext.md

**Title:** Announcing textual-plotext

**Path:** `blog/posts/textual-plotext.md`

**Content:**

```text
---
draft: false  
date: 2023-10-04

title: "Announcing textual-plotext"  
authors:
