#### workers.md

**Title:** Workers

**Path:** `guide/workers.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Workers

Textual's Worker API, introduced in version 0.18.0, simplifies concurrency management by enabling background execution of long-running tasks without blocking the UI.

## Concurrency

For operations that take significant time—such as network requests (`httpx`), subprocess I/O, or compute-heavy work—the UI must remain responsive. Textual's `run_worker` and `@work` decorator enable concurrent execution to prevent app lockups.

### Example: Network Request Pitfall
```python title="weather01.py"
--8<-- "docs/examples/guide/workers/weather01.py"
```
This example uses `httpx` to fetch weather data from `wttr.in`. However, synchronous request handling in a message handler blocks the UI until completion.

### Solution: Background Worker
```python title="weather02.py" hl_lines="21"
--8<-- "docs/examples/guide/workers/weather02.py"
```
Using `run_worker` schedules `update_weather` (an `async def`) in the background. It returns a `Worker[Coroutine]`, enabling concurrent execution without UI blocking.

> **Note**: The `exclusive=True` flag cancels prior workers, ensuring request responses are processed in order—preventing incorrect data display due to out-of-order results.

### Work Decorator
```python title="weather03.py" hl_lines="4 22 24"
--8<-- "docs/examples/guide/workers/weather03.py"
```
The `@work(exclusive=True)` decorator transforms an `async def` into a callable that spawns and starts a worker. No `await` is needed when calling the decorated function.

> **Note**: The decorator accepts same parameters as `run_worker`.

### Worker Return Values
- Access via `worker.result`: initially `None`, updated on completion.
- Use `worker.wait()` (a coroutine) to await result—but avoid in message handlers, as it blocks UI updates.
- Prefer handling [`Worker.StateChanged`](#worker-events) events for non-blocking access.

### Cancelling Workers
Call `worker.cancel()` at any time. This raises a `CancelledError` within the worker’s coroutine, causing early termination.

### Worker Errors
By default, exceptions terminate the app with traceback. Set `exit_on_error=False` in `run_worker` or `@work` to suppress this and allow recovery.

### Worker Lifetime & Management
Workers are managed by a single [`WorkerManager`](textual.worker_manager.WorkerManager) instance accessible via `app.workers`. Workers are tied to their creation context (widget, screen, app), and automatically cleaned up on removal or exit.

#### State Lifecycle
`worker.state` is a [`WorkerState`](textual.worker.WorkerState) enum:
- `PENDING`: Created but not started.
- `RUNNING`: Executing.
- `CANCELLED`: Cancelled externally.
- `ERROR`: Threw exception; error stored in `worker.error`.
- `SUCCESS`: Completed successfully; result in `worker.result`.

States progress: `PENDING` → `RUNNING` → (`CANCELLED`, `ERROR`, or `SUCCESS`).

<div class="excalidraw">
--8<-- "docs/images/workers/lifetime.excalidraw.svg"
</div>

### Worker Events
On state change, a [`Worker.StateChanged`](textual.worker.Worker.StateChanged) event is dispatched to the originating widget.

Handle with:
```python title="weather04.py" hl_lines="4 40-42"
--8<-- "docs/examples/guide/workers/weather04.py"
```

Run via: `textual run weather04.py --dev`  
Events appear in Textual’s [console](./devtools.md#console).

### Thread Workers
For non-async APIs, use `run_worker` with a thread-safe function. The worker runs in a background thread and can return results safely.

> **Note**: Worker API supports both coroutines (for async I/O) and threads (for blocking operations).
```

# Centering in Textual

Textual simplifies centering elements via three distinct rules: `align`, `text-align`, and `content-align`.

## Widget Alignment (`align`)
Applies to containers; centers child widgets relative to edges.  
- `align: center middle` centers horizontally and vertically.
- Requires widget width/height < container size.

```python
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center01.py"
```

**Note**: Without constraints, a widget fills its container—no horizontal movement possible. Use border or background to visualize layout (e.g., `border: white`, `background: blue`).

### Example: Centered Widget
Set width to `auto` for content-fit sizing:

```python hl_lines="16"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center03.py"
```

## Text Alignment (`text-align`)
Centers text *within* a widget, line-by-line.  
- Default: left-aligned.
- Options: `left`, `right`, `center`, `justify`.

```python hl_lines="4 18 23"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center04.py"
```

Center text:

```python hl_lines="19"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center05.py"
```

## Content Alignment (`content-align`)
Positions content *within* a widget’s border area.  
- Default: top-aligned.
- Use `content-align: center middle` to vertically center content.

```python hl_lines="19"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center06.py"
```

For vertical-only alignment, use `content-align-vertical: middle`.

```python hl_lines="21"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center07.py"
```

## Multiple Widgets
- Apply `align: center middle` to parent container → centers all children relative to screen.
  
```python
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center08.py"
```

To center widgets *relative to each other*, wrap in a [`Center`][textual.containers.Center] container:

```python hl_lines="2 22 24"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/center10.py"
```

## Summary
- **Widget**: Use `align` on parent; widget must be smaller than container.
- **Text**: Use `text-align` per line.
- **Content**: Use `content-align` within widget border area.
- **Multiple widgets**: Use [`Center`][textual.containers.Center] for relative centering.
- **Debug tip**: Add borders to visualize alignment.

For help, see [help](../help.md).

# Design a Layout

Textual’s layout system supports diverse application designs. Use these steps to begin:

#### package-with-hatch.md

```text
# Package a Textual App with Hatch

Python apps can be distributed via [PyPI](https://pypi.org/) using `pip`. This is *packaging*. For Textual apps, packaging follows standard Python practices but requires command-line launchability.

!!! tip  
    Use [`textual-serve`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual-serve) as an alternative to packaging.

This guide uses [Hatch](https://github.com/pypa/hatch), a build tool for packaging. Other tools like Poetry are viable, but Hatch offers rich features and ease of use.

### Calculator Example

```{.textual path="examples/calculator.py" columns=100 lines=41 press="3,.,1,4,5,9,2,wait:400"}
```

Source: [`calculator.py`](https://github.com/Textualize/textual/blob/main/examples/calculator.py)

## Overview

Packaging is manageable after one iteration. The goal is to enable:

```bash
pip install textual-calculator
calculator
```

## Project Structure

See [textual-calculator-hatch](https://github.com/Textualize/textual-calculator-hatch) for the completed project.

### Directory Layout (from `hatch new "textual calculator"`)

```
textual-calculator/
├── LICENSE.txt
├── README.md
├── pyproject.toml
├── src/
│   └── textual_calculator/
│       ├── __about__.py
│       └── __init__.py
└── tests/
    └── __init__.py
```

- `LICENSE.txt`: Project license.
- `README.md`: Project documentation (PyPI/GitHub).
- `pyproject.toml`: TOML metadata for packaging configuration.
- `src/textual_calculator/__about__.py`: Version number; update on release.
- `src/textual_calculator/__init__.py`, `tests/__init__.py`: Mark directories as Python packages.

The `src` directory contains the project’s module (`textual_calculator`) — importable via `import textual_calculator`. The top-level name uses hyphens (`textual-calculator`), while the module uses underscores (`textual_calculator`) due to Python import rules.

### Existing Code?

Use `hatch new --init <PROJECT NAME>` in an existing project to generate `pyproject.toml`. Prefer moving code into the standard structure once for consistency.

## Add App Code

Place source files under `src/<PROJECT_NAME>`. For the calculator:

```
textual-calculator/
├── src/textual_calculator/
│   ├── __about__.py
│   ├── __init__.py
│   ├── calculator.py
│   └── calculator.tcss
```

## Dependencies

In `pyproject.toml`, under `[project]`:

```toml
[project]
name = "textual-calculator"
dynamic = ["version"]
description = 'A example app'
readme = "README.md"
requires-python = ">=3.8"
license = "MIT"
keywords = []
authors = [
  { name = "Will McGugan", email = "redacted@textualize.io" },
]
classifiers = [
  "Development Status :: 4 - Beta",
  "Programming Language :: Python",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.8",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.9",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.10",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.11",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.12",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: Implementation :: CPython",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: Implementation :: PyPy",
]
dependencies = ["textual==0.47.1"]
```

`dependencies` lists required packages (e.g., `textual==0.47.1`). Version pinning ensures reproducibility.
## Virtual Environments

Use virtual environments to isolate dependencies per project. Create one with:

```bash
hatch env create
```

Activate via `hatch shell` or `hatch run`. Environment persists after creation.

#### render-and-compose.md

**Title:** Render and compose

**Path:** `how-to/render-and-compose.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Render and Compose

A common question on the [Textual Discord server](https://discord.gg/Enf6Z3qhVr) is the difference between [`render`][textual.widget.Widget.render] and [`compose`][textual.widget.Widget.compose]. This article clarifies their roles and demonstrates combined usage.

## Method Differences

- `render`: Returns a [Rich renderable](https://rich.readthedocs.io/en/latest/) (e.g., `str`, `Text`, `Table`) to define the widget’s background. Combined with CSS styles, rendered within borders.
- `compose`: Builds [*compound widgets*](../guide/widgets.md#compound-widgets) from nested widgets. If implemented, `render` is optional.

### Key Rule:
If both are defined, `render` sets the *background*, and `compose` adds child widgets on top.

## Combined Usage Example

Create a `Splash` widget with an animated linear gradient background and overlayed text:

=== "render_compose.py"

```python
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/render_compose.py"
```

1. Refreshes 30 times/sec.
2. Composes a single `Static` child.
3. Renders a [`LinearGradient`](textual.renderables.gradient.LinearGradient) background.

=== "Output"

```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/render_compose.py" columns="100" lines="40"}
```

!!! tip

    Animated gradients may be distracting; use sparingly.

## Summary

When building custom widgets:
1. Use `render` for simple renderables (text, Rich objects).
2. Use `compose` to compose compound widgets.
3. If both are defined, `render` provides the background layer.

We’re here to [help](../help.md)!  
  # Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/render_compose.py"
    
```

#### style-inline-apps.md

```text
# Style Inline Apps

Textual v0.55.0 introduces inline app execution below the prompt via `inline=True` in [`run()`][textual.app.App.run].

Most apps run inline unmodified, but CSS tweaks are available using the `:inline` pseudo-selector.

### Example: Dynamic Clock (Inline)
```python hl_lines="31"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/inline01.py"
```
- `inline=True` enables inline mode.
- Default layout: 5 lines (3 digits, 2 borders), plus 1 blank line above due to padding.

!!! note
    Set `INLINE_PADDING = 0` on your app class to remove default top padding.

### Customization via CSS
```python hl_lines="11-17"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/inline02.py"
```
Targets inline mode using `:inline`:
- `height: N` sets line count consumed.
- `border: none` removes default border.
- Color changes applied conditionally in inline context.

## Summary
Minimal app modifications needed for inline mode. Use `:inline` CSS rules to adjust height, borders, and styling.
```

#### work-with-containers.md

**Title:** Save time with Textual containers

**Path:** `how-to/work-with-containers.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Save Time with Textual Containers

Textual's [containers][textual.containers] provide reusable, styled compound widgets for arranging children. Not to be confused with [containerization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containerization_(computing)).

## What Are Containers?

Containers are compound widgets with preset styles that layout their children:
- [`Horizontal`][textual.containers.Horizontal]: arranges children in a horizontal row.
- [`Vertical`][textual.containers.Vertical]: stacks children vertically (top to bottom).

### Example: Horizontal Layout
```python hl_lines="2 21"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers01.py"
```
*Widgets yielded within `Horizontal` are placed right of prior widgets, forming a row. Behavior persists on dynamic updates.*

**Output:**  
```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers01.py"}```

### Implementation
```python
class Horizontal(Widget):
    """An expanding container with horizontal layout and no scrollbars."""

    DEFAULT_CSS = """
    Horizontal {
        width: 1fr;
        height: 1fr;
        layout: horizontal;
        overflow: hidden hidden;
    }
    """
```
Other containers follow the same minimal pattern.

## Layout Behavior

### Size & Expansion
- `Horizontal` and `Vertical` expand to fill available space.
- Use `with-border` class for visualizing container dimensions:
  ```python
  --8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers03.py"
  ```
  **Output:**  
  ```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers03.py"} ```

- Multiple containers divide screen space proportionally (e.g., two `Horizontal` → split in half).
- Use [FR units](../guide/styles.md#fr-units) for custom proportional layout.

### Group Containers
[`HorizontalGroup`][textual.containers.HorizontalGroup] and [`VerticalGroup`][textual.containers.VerticalGroup] do not expand to fill space:
```python hl_lines="2 27 31"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers05.py"
```
**Output:**  
```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers05.py"} ```

*Children are arranged horizontally, but container height matches content.*

## Scrolling Containers

Default containers do not scroll:
```python hl_lines="28 29"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers06.py"
```
**Output:**  
```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers06.py"} ```

*Excess content is clipped off-screen.*

Use [`HorizontalScroll`][textual.containers.HorizontalScroll] or [`VerticalScroll`][textual.containers.VerticalScroll] for auto-scrollbars:
```python hl_lines="2 27"
--8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers07.py"
```
**Output:**  
```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers07.py"} ```

*Scrollbar enables viewing all content.*

> ✅ Use `overflow` style for automatic scrollbars.

## Alignment Containers

- [`Center`][textual.containers.Center]: horizontally centers children.
- [`Right`][textual.containers.Right]: aligns children to right edge (left is default).
  ```python hl_lines="2 28 30"
  --8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers08.py"
  ```
  **Output:**  
  ```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers08.py"} ```

- [`Middle`][textual.containers.Middle]: vertically centers children:
  ```python hl_lines="2 27"
  --8<-- "docs/examples/how-to/containers09.py"
  ```
  **Output:**  
  ```{.textual path="docs/examples/how-to/containers09.py"} ```

> ✅ Set alignment via [align](../styles/align.md) rule in TCSS.

## Other Containers

Full list available at [container reference][textual.containers]. New containers may be added in future versions.

## Custom Containers

Extend `Widget` and define `DEFAULT_CSS`:
```python
class MyContainer(Widget):
    """My custom container."""
    DEFAULT_CSS = """
    MyContainer {
        # Your rules here
    }
    """
```

## Summary

- Containers are compound widgets for layout.
- Use `Horizontal`, `Vertical`, `Group`, `Scroll`, and alignment containers based on needs.
- All API signatures, class hierarchies, types, and terminology preserved.

hide:

<!-- Auto-generated by FAQtory -->
<!-- Do not edit by hand! -->

# Frequently Asked Questions

Welcome to the Textual FAQ. For unresolved queries, see [help](./help.md).

<a name="does-textual-support-images"></a>
## Does Textual support images?

No built-in image support yet; tracked on the [Roadmap](https://textual.textualize.io/roadmap/). Use [`rich-pixels`](https://github.com/darrenburns/rich-pixels) for Rich renderable image integration.

<a name="how-can-i-fix-importerror-cannot-import-name-composeresult-from-textualapp-"></a>
## ImportError: cannot import name ComposeResult from textual.app?

Upgrade to latest version:
```bash
pip install textual-dev -U
```

<a name="how-can-i-select-and-copy-text-in-a-textual-app"></a>
## How to select and copy text in a Textual app?

Textual supports click-drag selection on most widgets; use `Ctrl+C` to copy. For unsupported widgets, leverage terminal-specific modifiers:
- **iTerm**: Hold OPTION
- **Gnome Terminal**: Hold SHIFT
- **Windows Terminal**: Hold SHIFT  
See your terminal’s docs for details.

<a name="how-can-i-set-a-translucent-app-background"></a>
## How to set translucent app background?

Terminal translucency requires ANSI background colors, which Textual avoids. Textual uses 16.7M color mode for cross-platform consistency and advanced effects. See [Why no ANSI Themes?](#why-doesnt-textual-support-ansi-themes).

<a name="how-do-i-center-a-widget-in-a-screen"></a>
## How to center a widget in a screen?

Use `align: center middle` on the container (not the child). For individual centering, wrap each widget in [`Center`](https://textual.textualize.io/api/containers/#textual.containers.Center).

Example:
```python
from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
from textual.containers import Center
from textual.widgets import Button

class ButtonApp(App):
    CSS = """
    Screen {
        align: center middle;
    }
    """

    def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
        yield Center(Button("PUSH ME!"))
        yield Center(Button("AND ME!"))
        yield Center(Button("ALSO PLEASE PUSH ME!"))
        yield Center(Button("HEY ME ALSO!!"))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    ButtonApp().run()
```

<a name="how-do-i-fix-workerdeclarationerror"></a>
## How to fix WorkerDeclarationError?

Textual 0.31.0 requires `thread=True` for threaded workers:
```python
@work(thread=True)
def run_in_background():
    ...
```
For non-threaded, use async:
```python
@work()
async def run_in_background():
    ...
```

<a name="how-do-i-pass-arguments-to-an-app"></a>
## How to pass arguments to an app?

Override `__init__` in your App class:
```python
from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
from textual.widgets import Static

class Greetings(App[None]):
    def __init__(self, greeting: str="Hello", to_greet: str="World") -> None:
        self.greeting = greeting
        self.to_greet = to_greet
        super().__init__()

    def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
        yield Static(f"{self.greeting}, {self.to_greet}")

# Usage:
Greetings().run()
Greetings(to_greet="davep").run()
Greetings("Well hello", "there").run()
```

<a name="why-do-some-key-combinations-never-make-it-to-my-app"></a>
## Why some key combos don’t reach my app?

Only terminal-passed keys are available. Stick to universally supported:
- Letters, numbers
- F1–F10
- Space, Return
- Arrow, Home, End, Page
- Ctrl, Shift  
Avoid `Cmd`, `Option` (macOS), `Windows` key (Win). Test via `textual keys`.

<a name="why-doesnt-textual-look-good-on-macos"></a>
## Why Textual looks poor on macOS?

macOS Terminal.app may misrender box characters. Fix by adjusting font settings:
- Font: **Menlo Regular**
- Character spacing: 1
- Line spacing: 0.805  
Adjust line spacing for other fonts.
```

#### getting_started.md

```text
All you need to start building Textual apps.

## Requirements

Textual requires Python 3.9+ (prefer latest). Supports Linux, macOS, Windows, and any OS with Python.

### :fontawesome-brands-linux: Linux  
All distros support terminal-based execution; see [Linux console](./linux-console.md) for console-specific setup.

### :material-apple: macOS  
Default terminal limited to 256 colors. Recommend: iterm2, Ghostty, Kitty, or WezTerm.

### :material-microsoft-windows: Windows  
Use [Windows Terminal](https://apps.microsoft.com/store/detail/windows-terminal/9N0DX20HK701?hl=en-gb&gl=GB).

## Installation

### PyPI
```bash
pip install textual
```
For development:
```bash
pip install textual-dev
```
Enable syntax highlighting in `TextArea`:
```bash
pip install "textual[syntax]"
```

### conda-forge (via micromamba)
```bash
micromamba install -c conda-forge textual
```
Dev tools:
```bash
micromamba install -c conda-forge textual-dev
```

### Textual CLI  
Available if `textual-dev` installed. List commands:
```bash
textual --help
```
See [devtools](guide/devtools.md) for details.

## Demo

Run:
```bash
python -m textual
```

## Examples

Clone repository:
=== "HTTPS"
    ```bash
    git clone https://github.com/Textualize/textual.git
    ```
=== "SSH"
    ```bash
    git clone git@github.com:Textualize/textual.git
    ```
=== "GitHub CLI"
    ```bash
    gh repo clone Textualize/textual
    ```

Navigate to examples:
```bash
cd textual/examples/
python code_browser.py ../
```

Widget example source code (screenshots) in `docs/examples`.

See [help](./help.md) for support or bug reporting.

# Welcome

Welcome to the [Textual](https://github.com/Textualize/textual) framework documentation.

[Get started](./getting_started.md){ .md-button .md-button--primary } | [Tutorial](./tutorial.md)

## What is Textual?

Textual is a *Rapid Application Development* framework for Python, developed by [Textualize.io](https://www.textualize.io).  
Build complex UIs with a simple Python API. Run apps in the terminal or via web browser ([textual-serve](https://github.com/Textualize/textual-serve)).

<div class="grid cards" markdown>
- :material-clock-fast:{ .lg .middle } :material-language-python:{ .lg .middle } **Rapid development**  
  —— Uses existing Python skills for rich UIs.
- :material-raspberry-pi:{ .lg .middle } **Low requirements**  
  —— Runs on single-board computers.
- :material-microsoft-windows:{ .lg .middle } :material-apple:{ .lg .middle } :fontawesome-brands-linux:{ .lg .middle } **Cross-platform**  
  —— Works everywhere.
- :material-network:{ .lg .middle } **Remote**  
  —— Apps run over SSH.
- :fontawesome-solid-terminal:{ .lg .middle } **CLI Integration**  
  —— Launch and execute from command line.
- :material-scale-balance:{ .lg .middle } **Open Source**  
  —— MIT licensed.
</div>

---

# Built with Textual

Textual powers a growing ecosystem of developer and non-developer tools.

## Toad
Terminal frontend for AI coding tools (e.g., OpenHands, Claude Code, Gemini CLI).  
[Website](https://batrachian.ai) | [GitHub](https://github.com/batrachianai/toad)

```text
# Linux Console

The Linux console is less graphically capable than the terminal emulator on your desktop.

If you find your app does not look great with the default configuration, see [font-for-textual](https://github.com/jsatchell/font-for-textual) for a possible solution.
```

# Roadmap

Textual ([textualize.io](https://www.textualize.io/)) actively develops and maintains Textual. This page tracks ongoing work.

## Features

High-level features in development:

- [ ] Accessibility  
  * [ ] Screen reader integration  
  * [x] Monochrome mode  
  * [ ] High contrast theme  
  * [ ] Color-blind themes  
- [X] Command palette  
  * [X] Fuzzy search  
- [ ] Configuration (`.toml`-based extensible format)  
- [x] Console  
- [ ] Devtools  
  * [ ] Integrated log  
  * [ ] DOM tree view  
  * [ ] REPL  
- [ ] Reactive state abstraction  
- [x] Themes  
  * [ ] Configurable customization  
  * [ ] Built-in theme editor  

## Widgets

Core UI components with broad coverage. Planned or implemented:

- [x] Buttons  
  * [x] Error/warning variants  
- [ ] Color picker  
- [X] Checkbox  
- [X] Content switcher  
- [x] DataTable  
  * [x] Cell selection  
  * [x] Row/column selection  
  * [x] API for cell/row updates  
  * [ ] Lazy loading support  
- [ ] Date picker  
- [ ] Dropdown menus  
- [ ] Form widget  
  * [ ] Serialization/deserialization  
  * [ ] Export to `attrs` objects  
  * [ ] Export to `Pydantic` objects  
- [ ] Image support  
  * [ ] Half block rendering  
  * [ ] Braille  
  * [ ] Sixels and other image extensions  
- [x] Input  
  * [x] Validation  
  * [ ] Error/warning states  
  * [ ] Template types: IP, physical units (weight/volume), currency, credit card  
- [X] Select control (pull-down)  
- [X] Markdown viewer  
  * [ ] Collapsible sections  
  * [ ] Custom widget support  
- [ ] Plots  
  * [ ] Bar chart  
  * [ ] Line chart  
  * [ ] Candlestick charts  
- [X] Progress bars  
  * [ ] Style variants (solid, thin)  
- [X] Radio boxes  
- [X] Spark lines  
- [X] Switch  
- [X] Tabs  
- [X] TextArea (multi-line input)  
  * [X] Basic controls  
  * [ ] Indentation guides  
  * [ ] Language-aware smart features  
  * [X] Syntax highlighting

# Tutorial

Welcome to the Textual Tutorial — build fully featured apps with minimal boilerplate.

> *“If you want people to build things, make it fun.”*  
> &mdash; Will McGugan (creator of Rich and Textual)

## Video Series

[Accompanying video series](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLHhDR_Q5Me1MxO4LmfzMNNQyKfwa275Qe) covers this content.

## Stopwatch App Overview

Build a stopwatch app with:
- Multiple stopwatches
- Start, stop, reset controls per instance
- Dynamic addition/removal of stopwatches  
- Fully distributable design

Final UI:

```{.textual path="docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch.py" title="stopwatch.py" press="tab,enter,tab,enter,tab,enter,tab,enter"}
```

> `^p palette` enables [Command Palette](./guide/command_palette.md) — app-specific command prompt.

### Get the Code

Install Textual → clone repo:

=== "HTTPS"
```bash
git clone https://github.com/Textualize/textual.git
```

=== "SSH"
```bash
git clone git@github.com:Textualize/textual.git
```

=== "GitHub CLI"
```bash
gh repo clone Textualize/textual
```

Run:
```bash
cd textual/docs/examples/tutorial && python stopwatch.py
```

## Type Hints (Brief)

Type hints are optional in Textual. Used for static analysis via tools like `mypy`.

Example:
```python
def repeat(text: str, count: int) -> str:
    """Repeat string `count` times."""
    return text * count
```
- `param: type`: parameter typing (e.g., `text: str`)
- `-> type`: return typing (e.g., `-> str`)

## App Class Foundation

Extend `App` to create a Textual app:

```python title="stopwatch01.py"
--8<-- "docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch01.py"
```

Run:
```{.textual path="docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch01.py" title="stopwatch01.py"}
```
- `d`: toggle theme
- `ctrl+q`: exit

### App Class Breakdown

```python title="stopwatch01.py" hl_lines="1 2"
--8<-- "docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch01.py"
```

- `App` is the base class for all apps.
- Import `Header`, `Footer` from built-in widgets (display top/bottom bars).
- Widgets manage UI regions; custom ones are defined via composition.

#### Key Components

```python title="stopwatch01.py" hl_lines="5-19"
--8<-- "docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch01.py"
```

- `BINDINGS`: list of `(key, action_name, description)` tuples.  
  Example: `("d", "toggle_dark", "Toggle dark mode")`
- `compose()`: returns or yields widgets (generator preferred).  
  Returns `Header()` and `Footer()` in this case.
- `action_toggle_dark()`: action method (`action_` prefix) triggered by binding.

```python title="stopwatch01.py" hl_lines="22-24"
--8<-- "docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch01.py"
```

Final block:
```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    App().run()
```
→ Runs app in *application mode* until `ctrl+q`, safe for import or CLI execution.

## UI Design with Widgets

Use built-in widgets from [widget gallery](./widget_gallery.md).  
Customize via inheritance and composition.

### Sketch

<div class="excalidraw">
--8<-- "docs/images/stopwatch.excalidraw.svg"
</div>

### Custom Widget: `Stopwatch`

Extends `HorizontalGroup` to layout children horizontally. Components:
- `"Start"` Button
- `"Stop"` Button  
- `"Reset"` Button
- Time display (`Digits`)

```python title="stopwatch02.py" hl_lines="2-3 6-7 10-18 30"
--8<-- "docs/examples/tutorial/stopwatch02.py"
```

Imports:
- `Button`, `Digits`: for controls and time display
- `HorizontalGroup`, `VerticalScroll` from `textual.containers`: layout containers

> See [coordinating widgets](./guide/widgets.md#coordinating-widgets) for best practices.

#### Button Parameters

- `label`: displayed text (`"Start"`, etc.)
- `id`: unique identifier (for targeting in code/styles)
- `variant`: default style (`"success"` makes button green)

> All parameters preserved per API signature.

    dock: left;
}

    dock: left;
    display: none;
}

    dock: right;
}

    display: none
}

```

### `inline_python`

```
    def on_button_pressed(self, event: Button.Pressed) -> None:
        """Event handler called when a button is pressed."""
        button_id = event.button.id
        time_display = self.query_one(TimeDisplay)
        if button_id == "start":
            time_display.start()
            self.add_class("started")
        elif button_id == "stop":
            time_display.stop()
            self.remove_class("started")
        elif button_id == "reset":
            time_display.reset()

```

#### border_sub_title_align_all_example.md

**Title:** Border Sub Title Align All Example

**Path:** `snippets/border_sub_title_align_all_example.md`

**Content:**

```text
```markdown
This example demonstrates all border title and subtitle alignments, including custom Rich markup usage.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/border_sub_title_align_all.py"}

=== "border_sub_title_align_all.py"
    ```py hl_lines="6 20 26 32 41 42 44 47 53 59 65"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border_sub_title_align_all.py"

- Border (sub)titles support nested Rich markup.
- Long (sub)titles are truncated and occupy maximal space.
- (Sub)titles may be styled via Rich markup, including links.
- Empty (sub)titles are not rendered.
- If no border is set, titles/subtitles are hidden.
- When side borders are unset, (sub)title aligns with widget edge.
- Left-aligned long titles/subtitles truncate and show rightmost border character.
- Centered long titles/subtitles truncate symmetrically with 1-char padding.
- Right-aligned long titles/subtitles truncate and show leftmost border character.
- Utility function provided to generate labels with bordered title/subtitle.

=== "border_sub_title_align_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="12 16 30 34 41 46"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border_sub_title_align_all.tcss"

- Default title alignment: `left`; default subtitle alignment: `right`.
- Alignment has no effect on overly long (sub)titles unless shortened or widget widened.
- Empty (sub)titles are unaffected by alignment settings.
- No border (`none`/`hidden`) → (sub)title hidden.
- If alignment side lacks a border edge, (sub)title is flush to that side.
- (Sub)title positioning respects padding.
```
```

#### see_also_border.md

**Title:** See Also Border

**Path:** `snippets/see_also_border.md`

**Content:**

```text
- `border-title-align` → sets title alignment  
- `border-title-color` → sets title color  
- `border-title-background` → sets title background color  
- `border-title-style` → sets title text style  

- `border-subtitle-align` → sets subtitle alignment  
- `border-subtitle-color` → sets subtitle color  
- `border-subtitle-background` → sets subtitle background color  
- `border-subtitle-style` → sets subtitle text style

#### align.md

**Title:** Align

**Path:** `styles/align.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Align

The `align` style controls child widget positioning within a container.

## Syntax

```css
align: <horizontal> <vertical>;
align-horizontal: <horizontal>;
align-vertical: <vertical>;
```

Applies to containers; sets alignment for children.  
`<horizontal>` and `<vertical>` are defined in [`../css_types/horizontal.md`](../css_types/horizontal.md) and [`../css_types/vertical.md`](../css_types/vertical.md), respectively.

## Examples

### Basic Usage
Center two labels using `align: center middle;`.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/align.py"}
    ```

=== "align.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/align.py"
    ```

=== "align.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="2"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/align.tcss"
    ```

### All Alignments
3×3 grid with each cell using a different `align` value.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/align_all.py"}
    ```

=== "align_all.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/align_all.py"
    ```

=== "align_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30 34"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/align_all.tcss"
    ```

## CSS
```css
/* Center children */
align: center middle;
/* Top-right alignment */
align: right top;

/* Axis-specific alignment */
align-horizontal: right;
align-vertical: middle;
```

## Python
```python
# Center children
widget.styles.align = ("center", "middle")
# Top-right alignment
widget.styles.align = ("right", "top")

# Set axis alignment individually
widget.styles.align_horizontal = "right"
widget.styles.align_vertical = "middle"
```

## See also

- [`content-align`](./content_align.md): aligns content within a widget.
- [`text-align`](./text_align.md): aligns text inside a widget.

align: right top;

/* Change the horizontal alignment of the children of a widget */
align-horizontal: right;
/* Change the vertical alignment of the children of a widget */
align-vertical: middle;

```

### `inline_python`

widget.styles.align = ("center", "middle")

# Background

Sets the background color of a widget.

## Syntax

```css
background: <color> [<percentage>];
```

Requires a `<color>` optionally followed by `<percentage>` to define opacity (clamped 0%–100%).

## Examples

### Basic Usage

Creates three widgets with distinct backgrounds.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/background.py"}
    ```

=== "background.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background.py"
    ```

=== "background.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="9 13 17"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background.tcss"
    ```

### Opacity Variants

Displays ten side-by-side widgets demonstrating varying opacity levels.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/background_transparency.py"}
    ```

=== "background_transparency.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_transparency.py"
    ```

=== "background_transparency.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30 34 38"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_transparency.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Blue background */
background: blue;

/* 20% red background */
background: red 20%;

/* RGB color */
background: rgb(100, 120, 200);

/* HSL color */
background: hsl(290, 70%, 80%);
```

## Python

Same syntax as CSS; alternatively use `Color` objects.

```python
# Blue background
widget.styles.background = "blue"
# HSL-based color
widget.styles.background = "hsl(351,32%,89%)"

from textual.color import Color
# Parse string to Color
widget.styles.background = Color.parse("pink")
widget.styles.background = Color.parse("#FF00FF")
# Direct instantiation
widget.styles.background = Color(120, 60, 100)
```

## See also

- [`background-tint`](./background_tint.md) – blend color with background  
- [`color`](./color.md) – set text color

## Embedded Code Examples

    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background.py"
    
```

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_transparency.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Blue background */
background: blue;

/* 20% red background */
background: red 20%;

/* RGB color */
background: rgb(100, 120, 200);

/* HSL color */
background: hsl(290, 70%, 80%);

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Set blue background
widget.styles.background = "blue"
# Set through HSL model
widget.styles.background = "hsl(351,32%,89%)"

from textual.color import Color
# Set with a color object by parsing a string
widget.styles.background = Color.parse("pink")
widget.styles.background = Color.parse("#FF00FF")
# Set with a color object instantiated directly
widget.styles.background = Color(120, 60, 100)

```

#### background_tint.md

**Title:** Background-tint

**Path:** `styles/background_tint.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Background-tint

The `background-tint` style blends the background with a specified color, modifying it subtly for emphasis. Typically used on focused widgets to lighten the background.

```css
MyWidget:focus {
    background-tint: white 10%;
}
```

Tint opacity (alpha) should be < 100% to preserve original background; at 100%, tint fully replaces background.

## Syntax

--8<-- "docs/snippets/syntax_block_start.md"
background-tint: <a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a> [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
--8<-- "docs/snippets/syntax_block_end.md"

Requires a `<color>` with optional `<percentage>` for alpha (clamped 0%–100%).

## Examples

### Basic usage

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/background_tint.py"}
    ```

=== "background_tint.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_tint.py"
    ```

=== "background.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="5-9"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_tint.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* 10% background tint */
background-tint: blue 10%;

/* 20% RGB with alpha */
background-tint: rgb(100, 120, 200, 0.2);
```

## Python

Same syntax as CSS; alternatively use `Color` object for precise control.

```python
# 20% blue tint
widget.styles.background_tint = "blue 20%"

from textual.color import Color
# Explicit color with alpha
widget.styles.background_tint = Color(120, 60, 100, 0.5)
```

## See also

- [`background`](./background.md) – sets widget background color  
- [`color`](./color.md) – sets text color

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_css`

```
MyWidget:focus {
    background-tint: white 10%
}

```

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/background_tint.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* 10% backgrouhnd tint */

/* 20% RGB color */
background-tint: rgb(100, 120, 200, 0.2);

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Set 20% blue background tint
widget.styles.background_tint = "blue 20%"

from textual.color import Color
# Set with a color object
widget.styles.background_tint = Color(120, 60, 100, 0.5)

```

#### border.md

**Title:** Border

**Path:** `styles/border.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Border

The `border` style draws a box around a widget. Individual edges may be styled using `border-top`, `border-right`, `border-bottom`, and `border-left`.

!!! note  
    [`border`](./border.md) and [`outline`](./outline.md) cannot coexist on the same edge.

## Syntax

```css
border: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
border-top: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
border-right: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
border-bottom: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
border-left: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/percentage">&lt;percentage&gt;</a>];
```

In CSS, `border` is defined by a [border style](./border.md) and color (both optional), with an optional percentage for blending the border with background. In Python, use a tuple of (`border_style`, `color`).

## Border Command

Explore border types interactively via:

```bash
textual borders
```

See examples below.

## Examples

### Basic Usage

Three widgets with distinct border styles.

=== "Output"  
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/border.py"}  

=== "border.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border.py"

=== "border.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="4 10 16"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border.tcss"

### All Border Types

Grid displaying all available border types.

=== "Output"  
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/border_all.py"}  

=== "border_all.py"
    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border_all.py"

=== "border_all.tcss"
    ```css
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/border_all.tcss"

### Borders vs Outlines

--8<-- "docs/snippets/border_vs_outline_example.md"

## CSS

```css
/* Heavy white border */
border: heavy white;

/* Red left edge border */
border-left: outer red;

/* Rounded orange border, 50% opacity */
border: round orange 50%;
```

## Python

```python
# Heavy white border
widget.styles.border = ("heavy", "white")

# Red left border
widget.styles.border_left = ("outer", "red")
```

## See Also

- [`box-sizing`](./box_sizing.md): Controls how border affects widget dimensions.
- [`outline`](./outline.md): Adds an outline around widget content.

#### box_sizing.md

**Title:** Box-sizing

**Path:** `styles/box_sizing.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Box-sizing

The `box-sizing` style controls how width and height are computed.

## Syntax

```css
box-sizing: border-box | content-box;
```

### Values

- `border-box` (default): Padding and border included in dimensions. Content area shrinks when padding/border added.
- `content-box`: Padding and border increase widget size; content area remains fixed.

## Example

Both widgets are 5 units tall.  
Top: `box-sizing: border-box` — padding/border reduce content space.  
Bottom: `box-sizing: content-box` — padding/border expand total size.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/box_sizing.py"}
    ```

=== "box_sizing.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/box_sizing.py"
    ```

=== "box_sizing.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="2 6"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/box_sizing.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Default: border-box */
box-sizing: border-box;

/* Alternative: content-box */
box-sizing: content-box;
```

## Python

```python
# Set to border-box (default)
widget.box_sizing = "border-box"

# Set to content-box
widget.box_sizing = "content-box"
```

## See also

- [`border`](./border.md) for widget borders  
- [`padding`](./padding.md) for internal spacing

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/box_sizing.py"
    
```

```

/* Set box sizing to content-box */

```

### `inline_python`

```

# Set box sizing to content-box

```

# Color

The `color` style sets a widget's text color.

## Syntax

```css
color: (<color> | auto) [<percentage>];
```

Requires a `<color>` followed by an optional `<percentage>` for opacity. Use `"auto"` to automatically select black or white text for optimal contrast against the background.

## Examples

### Basic usage  
Sets distinct colors across three widgets.

=== "Output"

=== "color.py"

/* RGB color */

/* Auto-contrast text */

# Using color object

#### content_align.md

**Title:** Content-align

**Path:** `styles/content_align.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Content-align

The `content-align` style aligns content _within_ a widget.

## Syntax

```css
content-align: <horizontal> <vertical>;
content-align-horizontal: <horizontal>;
content-align-vertical: <vertical>;
```

Where `<horizontal>` and `<vertical>` are defined in [`../css_types/horizontal.md`](../css_types/horizontal.md) and [`../css_types/vertical.md`](../css_types/vertical.md), respectively.

`content-align` accepts both axes simultaneously; `content-align-horizontal` and `content-align-vertical` target individual axes.

## Examples

### Basic Usage
Three vertically stacked labels with distinct content alignments:

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/content_align.py"}
    ```

=== "content_align.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/content_align.py"
    ```

=== "content_align.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="2 7-8 13"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/content_align.tcss"
    ```

### All Alignments
A 3×3 grid of labels, each with unique content alignment:

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/content_align_all.py"}
    ```

=== "content_align_all.py"
    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/content_align_all.py"
    ```

=== "content_align_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="2 5 8 11 14 17 20 23 26"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/content_align_all.tcss"
    ```

## CSS
```css
/* Center content within widget */
content-align: center middle;
/* Align to top-right corner */
content-align: right top;

/* Set horizontal alignment */
content-align-horizontal: right;
/* Set vertical alignment */
content-align-vertical: middle;
```

## Python
```python
# Center content in widget
widget.styles.content_align = ("center", "middle")
# Top-right alignment
widget.styles.content_align = ("right", "top")

# Horizontal only
widget.styles.content_align_horizontal = "right"
# Vertical only
widget.styles.content_align_vertical = "middle"
```

## See also

- [`align`](./align.md): aligns child widgets within a container.
- [`text-align`](./text_align.md): aligns text content within a widget.

#### display.md

**Title:** Display

**Path:** `styles/display.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Display

The `display` style controls widget visibility and space allocation.

## Syntax

```css
display: block | none;
```

### Values

| Value       | Description |
|-------------|------------|
| `block`     | Widget is rendered normally; space reserved. (default) |
| `none`      | Widget hidden; no space reserved. |

## Example

Second widget hidden via `"remove"` class setting `display: none`.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/display.py"}
    ```

=== "display.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/display.py"
    ```

=== "display.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="13"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/display.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Visible */
display: block;

/* Hidden */
display: none;
```

## Python

```python
# Hide widget
self.styles.display = "none"

# Show widget
self.styles.display = "block"
```

Shortcut via `Widget.display` property:
- `True`: show (equivalent to `"block"`)
- `False`: hide (equivalent to `"none"`)

```python
# Hide
widget.display = False

# Show
widget.display = True
```

## See also

 - [`visibility`](./visibility.md) – controls visual visibility without affecting layout.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/display.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Widget is shown */
display: block;

/* Widget is not shown */
display: none;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Hide the widget
self.styles.display = "none"

# Show the widget again
self.styles.display = "block"

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Hide the widget
widget.display = False

# Show the widget
widget.display = True

```

#### grid_columns.md

**Title:** Grid-columns

```text
# Grid-columns

The `grid-columns` style defines column widths in grids with `layout: grid`.

## Syntax

```css
grid-columns: <scalar>+;
```

Applies to widgets using `layout: grid`. Takes one or more [`<scalar>`](../../css_types/scalar.md), specifying column lengths. If fewer scalars than columns, they repeat cyclically; excess scalars are ignored.

## Example

Grid with 2 rows and 5 columns:
```css
grid-columns: 1fr 16 2fr;
```
- Columns 1 & 4: `1fr`  
- Columns 2 & 5: `16`  
- Column 3: `2fr`

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/grid_columns.py"}
    ```

=== "grid_columns.py"

    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_columns.py"
    ```

=== "grid_columns.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="3"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_columns.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* All columns: 50% width */
grid-columns: 50%;

/* Alternating: first column 1fr, second 2fr */
grid-columns: 1fr 2fr;
```

## Python

```py
grid.styles.grid_columns = "50%"
grid.styles.grid_columns = "1fr 2fr"
```

## See also

- [`grid-rows`](./grid_rows.md) for row height definition

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_columns.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Set all columns to have 50% width */
grid-columns: 50%;

/* Every other column is twice as wide as the first one */
grid-columns: 1fr 2fr;

```

### `inline_py`

```
grid.styles.grid_columns = "50%"
grid.styles.grid_columns = "1fr 2fr"

```

```

#### grid_gutter.md

**Content:**

```text
# Grid-gutter

Sets the gutter size in `grid` layout, defining spacing between adjacent cells.  
Applies only *between* cell edges; no padding is added between cells and container boundaries.

!!! note

    Applies exclusively to widgets with `layout: grid`.

## Syntax

```css
grid-gutter: <integer> [<integer>];
```

Takes one or two `<integer>` values:
- One value sets both vertical and horizontal gutters.
- Two values set vertical (first) and horizontal (second) gutters.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/grid_gutter.py"}
    ```

=== "grid_gutter.py"

    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_gutter.py"
    ```

=== "grid_gutter.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="3"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_gutter.tcss"
    ```

> *Uses double horizontal gutter to compensate for terminal cell aspect ratio (typically 2× taller than wide), achieving visually consistent spacing.*

## CSS

```css
/* Equal gutters */
grid-gutter: 5;

/* Separate vertical and horizontal gutters */
grid-gutter: 1 2;
```

## Python

Vertical and horizontal gutters are separate properties:

```py
widget.styles.grid_gutter_vertical = "1"
widget.styles.grid_gutter_horizontal = "2"
```

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_gutter.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Set vertical and horizontal gutters to be the same */
grid-gutter: 5;

/* Set vertical and horizontal gutters separately */
grid-gutter: 1 2;

```

### `inline_py`

```
widget.styles.grid_gutter_vertical = "1"
widget.styles.grid_gutter_horizontal = "2"

```

```

#### grid_size.md

**Title:** Grid-size

**Path:** `styles/grid/grid_size.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Grid-size

The `grid-size` style defines the number of columns and rows in a grid layout. The row count may be omitted, in which case it is computed automatically.

Applies only to widgets with `layout: grid`.

## Syntax

```
grid-size: <integer> [<integer>];
```

Takes one or two non-negative integers:
- First integer: number of columns.
- Second integer (optional): explicitly sets the number of rows, overriding automatic computation based on children.

## Examples

### Columns and Rows
```css
/* 2 cols, 4 rows */
grid-size: 2 4;
```

### Columns Only
```css
/* 2 cols, auto rows */
grid-size: 2;
```

## CSS
```css
/* 3 columns, 5 rows */
grid-size: 3 5;

/* 4 columns, auto rows */
grid-size: 4;
```

## Python API
Programmatically set grid size:
```py
widget.styles.grid_size_columns = 6
widget.styles.grid_size_rows = 3
```

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_size_both.py"
    
```

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/grid_size_columns.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Grid with 3 columns and 5 rows */
grid-size: 3 5;

/* Grid with 4 columns and as many rows as needed */
grid-size: 4;

```

### `inline_py`

```
widget.styles.grid_size_rows = 3
widget.styles.grid_size_columns = 6

```

```

# Grid

Styles for Textual's `grid` layout. For in-depth usage, see the [grid guide](../../guide/layout.md#grid).

| [`grid-columns`](./grid_columns.md) | Column widths (`<scalar>+`).                 |
| [`grid-gutter`](./grid_gutter.md)  | Spacing between cells (`<scalar>[<scalar>]`).|
| [`grid-rows`](./grid_rows.md)    | Row heights (`<scalar>+`).                   |
| [`grid-size`](./grid_size.md)    | Grid dimensions: columns and rows (`<integer>[<integer>]`). |
| [`row-span`](./row_span.md)     | Number of rows a cell spans (`<integer>`).   |

## Syntax

--8<-- "docs/snippets/syntax_block_start.md"

#### height.md

**Title:** Height

**Path:** `styles/height.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Height

The `height` style sets a widget's vertical dimension.

## Syntax

```css
height: <scalar>;
```

Requires a [`<scalar>`](../css_types/scalar.md). Default behavior: sets content area height; when [`box-sizing`](./box_sizing.md) is `border-box`, it affects border area.

## Examples

### Basic Usage

Sets widget height to 50% of screen:

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/height.py"}
    ```

=== "height.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/height.py"
    ```

=== "height.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="3"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/height.tcss"
    ```

### Height Formats

Demonstrates all supported units. Output includes vertical ruler for visual alignment.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/height_comparison.py" lines=24 columns=80}
    ```

=== "height_comparison.py"

    ```py hl_lines="17-25"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/height_comparison.py"
    ```

=== "height_comparison.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="2 5 8 11 14 17 20 23 26"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/height_comparison.tcss"
    ```

*   `2` → height = 2 lines  
*   `12.5%` → 12.5% of container (24 lines) = 3  
*   `5%` → 5% of direct container width (`VerticalScroll`, 80 cols) = 4  
*   `12.5%` → 12.5% of direct container height (`VerticalScroll`, 24 rows) = 3  
*   `6.25%` → 6.25% of viewport width (80 cols) = 5  
*   `12.5%` → 12.5% of viewport height (24 rows) = 3  
*   `auto` → optimal content fit; single-line content → height = 1  
*   `1fr` → half the height of a `2fr` element  
*   `2fr` → twice the height of a `1fr` element  

## CSS

```css
/* Explicit cell height */
height: 10;

/* Percentage height */
height: 50%;

/* Automatic height */
height: auto;
```

## Python

```python
self.styles.height = 10  # int for explicit cell height
self.styles.height = "50%"
self.styles.height = "auto"
```

## See Also

- [`max-height`](./max_height.md), [`min-height`](./min_height.md) – constrain widget height  
- [`width`](./width.md) – set horizontal dimension

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/height.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Explicit cell height */
height: 10;

/* Percentage height */
height: 50%;

/* Automatic height */
height: auto

```

### `inline_python`

```
self.styles.height = 10  # Explicit cell height can be an int
self.styles.height = "50%"
self.styles.height = "auto"

```

#### keyline.md

**Title:** Keyline

**Path:** `styles/keyline.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Keyline

The `keyline` style draws lines outside a container’s border, in its margin. Unlike `border`, keylines can overlap and cross to form dividing lines between child widgets.

Applies only to containers with layout; requires `margin` or `grid-gutter` for visible effect.

## Syntax

```css
keyline: [<a href="../../css_types/keyline">&lt;keyline&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
```

## Examples

### Horizontal Keyline

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/keyline_horizontal.py"}
    ```

=== "keyline.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/keyline_horizontal.py"

```text
# Layer

The `layer` style assigns a widget to a specific layer.

## Syntax

```css
layer: <name>;
```

Where `<name>` must correspond to a layer defined in a [`layers`](./layers.md) declaration by an ancestor. See [CSS types/name](../css_types/name.md).

!!! warning  
    Using an undefined `<name>` has no effect.

## Example

In the example, `#box1` is drawn on top of `#box2` despite being yielded earlier due to its higher layer.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.py"}
    ```

    --8<-- "docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.tcss"
    ```

```

## Python

#### layers.md

**Title:** Layers

**Path:** `styles/layers.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Layers

The `layers` style defines an ordered sequence of named layers, determining painting order.

## Syntax

```text
layers: <name>+;
```

Accepts one or more `<name>` values, which define the layer stack. Earlier-defined layers are drawn beneath later ones. These names can be referenced via the [`layer`](./layer.md) property.

See also: [layout guide (Layers)](../guide/layout.md#layers)

## Example

In this example, `#box1` is rendered before `#box2`, but appears on top due to being assigned a higher layer.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.py"}
    ```

=== "layers.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.py"
    ```

=== "layers.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="3 14 19"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Bottom layer: 'below'; top layer: 'above' */
layers: below above;
```

## Python

```python
# Set layer order via style attribute
widget.style.layers = ("below", "above")
```

## See also

- [Layout guide (Layers)](../guide/layout.md#layers)
- [`layer`](./layer.md) to assign a widget to a specific layer

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/guide/layout/layers.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Bottom layer is called 'below', layer above it is called 'above' */
layers: below above;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Bottom layer is called 'below', layer above it is called 'above'
widget.style.layers = ("below", "above")

```

```

# Layout

The `layout` style controls child widget arrangement.

### Syntax

```text
layout: grid | horizontal | vertical;
```

### Values

| Value          | Description |
|----------------|-------------|
| `grid`         | Arranges children in a grid. |
| `horizontal`   | Arranges children left to right along the horizontal axis. |
| `vertical` (default) | Arranges children top to bottom along the vertical axis. |

### Example

See [layout guide](../guide/layout.md) and [grid reference](./grid/index.md).

```text
# Links

Textual supports inline "links" in text that trigger actions on press. Styles affect their appearance within widgets.

!!! note  
    These CSS rules apply only to Textual action links; internet hyperlinks are unaffected.

| Property                     | Description                                      |
|------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
| `link-background`            | Background color of link text.                   |
| `link-background-hover`      | Background color when hovered.                   |
| `link-color`                 | Color of link text.                              |
| `link-color-hover`           | Color when hovered.                              |
| `link-style`                 | Text style (e.g., underline).                    |
| `link-style-hover`           | Style when hovered.                              |

## Syntax

```css
link-background: <color> [<percentage>];
link-color: <color> [<percentage>];
link-style: <text-style>;
link-background-hover: <color> [<percentage>];
link-color-hover: <color> [<percentage>];
link-style-hover: <text-style>;
```

See each property’s reference for value semantics.

## Example

=== "Output"  
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/links.py"}

# `link-background`

Sets the background color of Textual action links only — **not** regular hyperlinks.

```css
link-background: <color> [<percentage>];

Applies to [`<color>`](../../css_types/color.md) with optional opacity via [`<percentage>`](../../css_types/percentage.md). Only affects *action links* as defined in the [actions guide](../../guide/actions.md#links).

    ```

    Only affects action links; hyperlinks ignored.

#### margin.md

**Title:** Margin

**Path:** `styles/margin.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Margin

The `margin` style defines edge spacing around a widget.

## Syntax

```css
margin: <integer>;                    /* All edges */
      | <integer> <integer>;          /* Top/bottom, left/right */
      | <integer> <integer> <integer> <integer>;  /* Top, right, bottom, left */

margin-top: <integer>;
margin-right: <integer>;
margin-bottom: <integer>;
margin-left: <integer>;
```

- **1 value**: Applies same margin to all four edges.
- **2 values**: First applies to top/bottom; second to left/right.
- **4 values**: Applied clockwise: top → right → bottom → left (clockwise order).

## Examples

### Basic Usage
Sets large margin on a label, moving it from the top-left corner.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/margin.py"}
    ```

=== "margin.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin.py"
    ```

=== "margin.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="7"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin.tcss"
    ```

### All Margin Settings
Demonstrates margin variations in a grid layout.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/margin_all.py"}
    ```

=== "margin_all.py"
    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin_all.py"
    ```

=== "margin_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="25 29 33 37 41 45 49 53"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin_all.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* All edges: 1 */
margin: 1;

/* Top/bottom: 2; left/right: 4 */
margin: 2 4;

/* Top: 1, right: 2, bottom: 3, left: 4 */
margin: 1 2 3 4;

margin-top: 1;
margin-right: 2;
margin-bottom: 3;
margin-left: 4;
```

## Python

Python does not expose `margin-top`, `margin-right`, `margin-bottom`, or `margin-left`.  
Use:
- Integer for uniform margin.
- Tuple of 2 integers for top/bottom and left/right.
- Tuple of 4 integers for top, right, bottom, left.

```python
# Uniform margin
widget.styles.margin = 1

# Top/bottom: 2; left/right: 4
widget.styles.margin = (2, 4)

# Top: 1, right: 2, bottom: 3, left: 4
widget.styles.margin = (1, 2, 3, 4)
```

## See also

- [`padding`](./padding.md) for content spacing.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin.py"
    
```

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/margin_all.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Set margin of 1 around all edges */
margin: 1;
/* Set margin of 2 on the top and bottom edges, and 4 on the left and right */
margin: 2 4;
/* Set margin of 1 on the top, 2 on the right,
                 3 on the bottom, and 4 on the left */
margin: 1 2 3 4;

margin-top: 1;
margin-right: 2;
margin-bottom: 3;
margin-left: 4;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Set margin of 1 around all edges
widget.styles.margin = 1
# Set margin of 2 on the top and bottom edges, and 4 on the left and right
widget.styles.margin = (2, 4)
# Set margin of 1 on top, 2 on the right, 3 on the bottom, and 4 on the left
widget.styles.margin = (1, 2, 3, 4)

```

```

#### max_height.md

**Title:** Max-height

**Path:** `styles/max_height.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Max-height

Sets a maximum height for a widget.

## Syntax

```css
max-height: <scalar>;
```

Accepts a [`<scalar>`](../css_types/scalar.md) defining an upper bound on the widget's `height`. The actual height never exceeds this value.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/max_height.py"}
    ```

=== "max_height.py"

    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_height.py"
    ```

=== "max_height.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="12 16 20 24"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_height.tcss"
    ```

> Note: This has no effect if the widget’s height is already below `max-height`.

## CSS

```css
/* Maximum height: 10 rows */
max-height: 10;

/* Maximum height: 25% of viewport height */
max-height: 25vh;
```

## Python

```python
# Set max height to 10 rows
widget.styles.max_height = 10

# Set max height to 25% of viewport height
widget.styles.max_height = "25vh"
```

## See also

- [`min-height`](./min_height.md): sets a lower bound on widget height  
- [`height`](./height.md): sets the explicit height of a widget

## Embedded Code Examples

    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_height.py"

### `inline_css`

/* Set the maximum height to 25% of the viewport height */
max-height: 25vh;

```

### `inline_python`

```

# Set the maximum height to 25% of the viewport height

#### max_width.md

**Title:** Max-width

**Path:** `styles/max_width.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Max-width

The `max-width` style enforces an upper limit on a widget’s width.

## Syntax

```css
max-width: <scalar>;
```

Accepts a [`<scalar>`](../css_types/scalar.md) defining the maximum allowable width; the widget's actual width cannot exceed this value.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/max_width.py"}
    ```

=== "max_width.py"

    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_width.py"
    ```

=== "max_width.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="12 16 20 24"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_width.tcss"
    ```

> Note: This has no effect when the widget’s width is already below `max-width`.

## CSS

```css
/* Maximum width: 10 rows */
max-width: 10;

/* Maximum width: 25% of viewport width */
max-width: 25vw;
```

## Python

```python
# Set max width to 10 rows
widget.styles.max_width = 10

# Set max width to 25% of viewport width
widget.styles.max_width = "25vw"
```

## See also

- [`min-width`](./min_width.md) – sets minimum width  
- [`width`](./width.md) – sets explicit width

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/max_width.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Set the maximum width to 10 rows */
max-width: 10;

/* Set the maximum width to 25% of the viewport width */
max-width: 25vw;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Set the maximum width to 10 rows
widget.styles.max_width = 10

# Set the maximum width to 25% of the viewport width
widget.styles.max_width = "25vw"

```

```

# Min-height

Sets a minimum height for a widget.

## Syntax

```css
min-height: <scalar>;
```

Accepts a [`<scalar>`](../css_types/scalar.md) defining the lower bound for the widget's `height`. The actual height never falls below this value.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/min_height.py"}
    ```

    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/min_height.py"
    ```

    ```css hl_lines="13 17 21 25"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/min_height.tcss"
    ```

> Note: This has no effect if the widget’s height exceeds `min-height`.

## CSS

```css
/* Minimum height: 10 rows */

/* Minimum height: 25% of viewport height */
min-height: 25vh;
```

## Python

```python

#### offset.md

**Title:** Offset

**Path:** `styles/offset.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Offset

The `offset` style applies positional offset to a widget.

## Syntax

```css
offset: <scalar> <scalar>;
offset-x: <scalar>;
offset-y: <scalar>;
```

Where the two `<scalar>` values in `offset` specify horizontal and vertical offsets, respectively. Use `offset-x` or `offset-y` for single-axis offsetting.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/offset.py"}
    ```

=== "offset.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/offset.py"
    ```

=== "offset.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="13 20 27"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/offset.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Move widget 8 cells in x, 2 in y */
offset: 8 2;

/* Move widget 4 cells in x */
offset-x: 4;

/* Move widget -3 cells in y */
offset-y: -3;
```

## Python

Offset must be set for both axes simultaneously:

```python
# Set offset to (2, 4)
widget.styles.offset = (2, 4)
```

> **Note**: No per-axis setter method exists; `offset` is a tuple-only property.

## See also

- [Layout guide: Offsets](../guide/layout.md#offsets)

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/offset.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Move the widget 8 cells in the x direction and 2 in the y direction */
offset: 8 2;

/* Move the widget 4 cells in the x direction
offset-x: 4;
/* Move the widget -3 cells in the y direction
offset-y: -3;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Move the widget 2 cells in the x direction, and 4 in the y direction.
widget.styles.offset = (2, 4)

```

```

#### opacity.md

**Title:** Opacity

**Path:** `styles/opacity.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Opacity

The `opacity` style controls widget transparency. Though terminals lack true alpha blending, Textual approximates opacity by mixing widget colors with their background.

## Syntax

```css
opacity: <number> | <percentage>;
```

- `<number>`: 0.0 (fully transparent) to 1.0 (fully opaque).  
- `<percentage>`: 0% (transparent) to 100% (opaque).

Typical use cases include dimming widgets for *disabled* states—e.g., `opacity: 70%`.

## Example

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/opacity.py"}
    ```

=== "opacity.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/opacity.py"
    ```

=== "opacity.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="2 6 10 14 18"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/opacity.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Fade widget to 50% opacity against parent background */
opacity: 50%;
```

## Python

```python
# Set 50% opacity via style assignment
widget.styles.opacity = "50%"
```

## See also

- [`text-opacity`](./text_opacity.md): blends content color with background, independent of widget-level opacity.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/opacity.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Fade the widget to 50% against its parent's background */
opacity: 50%;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Fade the widget to 50% against its parent's background
widget.styles.opacity = "50%"

```

#### outline.md

**Title:** Outline

**Path:** `styles/outline.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Outline

The `outline` style draws a box **over** the content area of a widget.  
!!! note  
    [`border`](./border.md) and [`outline`](./outline.md) cannot coexist on the same edge.

## Syntax

```css
outline: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
outline-top: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
outline-right: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
outline-bottom: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
outline-left: [<a href="../../css_types/border">&lt;border&gt;</a>] [<a href="../../css_types/color">&lt;color&gt;</a>];
```

`outline` accepts optional `<border>` (style) and `<color>` (value).  
Unlike `border`, the outline is rendered **over** content.

## Border Command

Explore border types interactively via:
```bash
textual borders
```

## Examples

### Basic Usage

Widget with outline; outline occludes text area.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/outline.py"}
    ```

    ```python

    ```

=== "outline.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="8"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/outline.tcss"
    ```

### All Outline Types

Grid demonstrating all outline types.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/outline_all.py"}
    ```

=== "outline_all.py"
    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/outline_all.py"
    ```

=== "outline_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30 34 38 42 46 50 54 58"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/outline_all.tcss"
    ```

### Borders and Outlines

--8<-- "docs/snippets/border_vs_outline_example.md"

## CSS

```css
/* Heavy white outline */
outline: heavy white;

/* Red left-side outline */
outline-left: outer red;
```

## Python

```python
# Heavy white outline
widget.outline = ("heavy", "white")

# Red left outline
widget.outline_left = ("outer", "red")
```

## See Also

- [`border`](./border.md) for border styling.

```

### `inline_python`

```

# Set a red outline on the left
widget.outline_left = ("outer", "red")

#### overflow.md

**Title:** Overflow

**Path:** `styles/overflow.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Overflow

The `overflow` style controls when scrollbars are displayed.

## Syntax

```css
overflow: <a href="../../css_types/overflow">&lt;overflow&gt;</a> <a href="../../css_types/overflow">&lt;overflow&gt;</a>;
overflow-x: <a href="../../css_types/overflow">&lt;overflow&gt;</a>;
overflow-y: <a href="../../css_types/overflow">&lt;overflow&gt;</a>;
```

`overflow` accepts two values for horizontal and vertical overflow respectively.  
Individual axis control is available via `overflow-x` (horizontal) and `overflow-y` (vertical).

### Defaults

Default: `overflow: auto auto`.  
Note: Built-in containers like `Horizontal` and `VerticalScroll` override this.

## Example

Split screen into left/right; each has three vertically scrolling widgets exceeding terminal height.

- Left: `overflow-y: auto` → shows scrollbar automatically.
- Right: `overflow-y: hidden` → hides scrollbar.

=== "Output"

    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/overflow.py"}
    ```

=== "overflow.py"

    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/overflow.py"
    ```

=== "overflow.tcss"

    ```css hl_lines="19"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/overflow.tcss"
    ```

## CSS

```css
/* Auto scrollbars on both axes (default) */
overflow: auto auto;

/* Hide vertical scrollbar */
overflow-y: hidden;

/* Always show horizontal scrollbar */
overflow-x: scroll;
```

## Python

Cannot set both axes simultaneously.

```python
# Hide vertical scrollbar
widget.styles.overflow_y = "hidden"

# Always show horizontal scrollbar
widget.styles.overflow_x = "scroll"
```

# Limit input size for API calls

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/overflow.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Automatic scrollbars on both axes (the default) */
overflow: auto auto;

/* Hide the vertical scrollbar */
overflow-y: hidden;

/* Always show the horizontal scrollbar */
overflow-x: scroll;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Hide the vertical scrollbar
widget.styles.overflow_y = "hidden"

# Always show the horizontal scrollbar
widget.styles.overflow_x = "scroll"

```

#### padding.md

**Title:** Padding

**Path:** `styles/padding.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Padding

The `padding` style defines inner spacing around a widget’s content.

## Syntax

```css
padding: <integer>;                    /* All edges */
       | <integer> <integer>;          /* Top/bottom, left/right */
       | <integer> <integer> <integer> <integer>;  /* Top, right, bottom, left */

padding-top: <integer>;
padding-right: <integer>;
padding-bottom: <integer>;
padding-left: <integer>;
```

Values are integers specifying spacing in pixels.  
- 1 value: uniform padding on all edges.  
- 2 values: first for top/bottom, second for left/right.  
- 4 values: applied clockwise — top → right → bottom → left (clockwise order).  

Individual edge padding uses `padding-top`, `padding-right`, `padding-bottom`, and `padding-left`.

## Example

### Basic Usage
Adds padding around text.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/padding.py"}

=== "padding.py"
    ```python
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding.py"

=== "padding.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="7"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding.tcss"

### All Padding Settings
Demonstrates padding variations in a grid. Each cell’s placeholder uses different `padding` values, visible via colored background.

=== "Output"
    ```{.textual path="docs/examples/styles/padding_all.py"}

=== "padding_all.py"
    ```py
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding_all.py"

=== "padding_all.tcss"
    ```css hl_lines="16 20 24 28 32 36 40 44"
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding_all.tcss"

## CSS

```css
/* Uniform padding */
padding: 1;
/* Top/bottom = 2, left/right = 4 */
padding: 2 4;
/* Top=1, right=2, bottom=3, left=4 */
padding: 1 2 3 4;

padding-top: 1;
padding-right: 2;
padding-bottom: 3;
padding-left: 4;
```

## Python

Set `widget.styles.padding` using:
- Integer (all edges)
- Tuple of 2 integers (top/bottom, left/right)
- Tuple of 4 integers (top, right, bottom, left)

```python
# All edges = 1
widget.styles.padding = 1
# Top/bottom = 2, left/right = 4
widget.styles.padding = (2, 4)
# Top=1, right=2, bottom=3, left=4
widget.styles.padding = (1, 2, 3, 4)
```

## See also

- [`box-sizing`](./box_sizing.md) – controls how padding affects widget dimensions.  
- [`margin`](./margin.md) – adds spacing outside the widget.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_python`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding.py"
    
```

### `inline_py`

```
    --8<-- "docs/examples/styles/padding_all.py"
    
```

### `inline_css`

```
/* Set padding of 1 around all edges */
padding: 1;
/* Set padding of 2 on the top and bottom edges, and 4 on the left and right */
padding: 2 4;
/* Set padding of 1 on the top, 2 on the right,
                 3 on the bottom, and 4 on the left */
padding: 1 2 3 4;

padding-top: 1;
padding-right: 2;
padding-bottom: 3;
padding-left: 4;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Set padding of 1 around all edges
widget.styles.padding = 1
# Set padding of 2 on the top and bottom edges, and 4 on the left and right
widget.styles.padding = (2, 4)
# Set padding of 1 on top, 2 on the right, 3 on the bottom, and 4 on the left
widget.styles.padding = (1, 2, 3, 4)

```

#### pointer.md

**Title:** Pointer

**Path:** `styles/pointer.md`

**Content:**

```text
# Pointer

The `pointer` style defines the mouse cursor shape when hovering over a widget. Requires terminal support for the Kitty pointer shapes protocol; unsupported terminals will not change cursor appearance.

## Syntax

```css
pointer: <pointer>;
```

Accepts values from the [`<pointer>`](../css_types/pointer.md) type, specifying cursor shape.

### Defaults

Default value: `default`.

## Example

Built-in widgets and scrollbars use pointer styles. Run the Textual demo to observe changes (hover over buttons or drag a scrollbar):

```bash
python -m textual
```

## CSS

```css
/* Pointing hand */
pointer: pointer;

/* Text selection */
pointer: text;

/* Grab (drag) */
pointer: grab;

/* Crosshair */
pointer: crosshair;
```

## Python

```python
widget.styles.pointer = "pointer"
widget.styles.pointer = "text"
widget.styles.pointer = "grab"
widget.styles.pointer = "crosshair"
```

## See also

- [`<pointer>`](../css_types/pointer.md) data type for all available pointer shapes.

## Embedded Code Examples

### `inline_css`

```
/* Show a pointing hand cursor */
pointer: pointer;

/* Show a text selection cursor */
pointer: text;

/* Show a grab cursor */
pointer: grab;

/* Show a crosshair cursor */
pointer: crosshair;

```

### `inline_python`

```
# Show a pointing hand cursor
widget.styles.pointer = "pointer"

# Show a text selection cursor
widget.styles.pointer = "text"

# Show a grab cursor
widget.styles.pointer = "grab"

# Show a crosshair cursor
widget.styles.pointer = "crosshair"

```
